when you say she's a programmer , she did do some , but the real thing is to have said the future is going to be much , much more than this .	當你說她是程式設計師 , 她做了一些事 , 但真正要說的是 , 未來將會遠遠超過這個 。
now , a hundred years later , this guy comes along , alan turing , and in 1936 , and invents the computer all over again .	一百年後 , 這個傢伙出現了 , 艾倫•圖靈 , 1936年發明了電腦 。
now , of course , babbage's machine was entirely mechanical .	當然 , babbage的機器是完全機械的 。
turing's machine was entirely theoretical .	烏丁的機器完全是理論性的 。
both of these guys were coming from a mathematical perspective , but turing told us something very important .	兩者都來自數學觀點 , 但圖靈告訴我們一件非常重要的事 。
he laid down the mathematical foundations for computer science , and said , " it doesn't matter how you make a computer . "	他為電腦科學奠定了數學基礎 , 並說: 「 不管你怎麼製造電腦 。 」
it doesn't matter if your computer's mechanical , like babbage's was , or electronic , like computers are today , or perhaps in the future , cells , or , again , mechanical again , once we get into nanotechnology .	不論你的電腦的機械性 , 例如babbage , 或電子 , 像是現今的電腦 , 或在未來 , 細胞 , 或者 , 同樣的 , 一旦我們進入了奈米科技 。
we could go back to babbage's machine and just make it tiny . all those things are computers .	我們可以回到babbage的機器 , 把它做得很小 。 所有東西都是電腦 。
there is in a sense a computing essence .	在某種意義上 , 有一個計算的本質 。
this is called the church–turing thesis .	這叫做教堂在進行分析 。
and so suddenly , you get this link where you say this thing babbage had built really was a computer .	突然間 , 你就有了這個連結 , 你說這個東西babbage建了一台電腦 。
in fact , it was capable of doing everything we do today with computers , only really slowly .	事實上 , 它能夠用電腦來做我們現今所做的每件事 , 只有很慢 。
to give you an idea of how slowly , it had about 1k of memory .	為了讓你們知道它有多慢 , 大約1k的記憶 。
it used punch cards , which were being fed in , and it ran about 10 , 000 times slower the first zx81 .	它用了打孔卡 , 被吸進去 , 跑了大約一萬倍 , 最早的zx81 。
it did have a ram pack .	它的確有一堆ram包 。
you could add on a lot of extra memory if you wanted to .	若你想的話 , 你可以加入很多額外的記憶 。
so , where does that bring us today ?	所以 , 今天會帶我們到哪裡 ?
so there are plans .	所以 , 這裡有計畫 。
over in swindon , the science museum archives , there are hundreds of plans and thousands of pages of notes written by charles babbage about this analytical engine .	在瑞典 , 科學博物館的檔案 , 有數以千計的計劃和數以千計的筆記 , 由查爾斯•巴比奇所寫的 。
one of those is a set of plans that we call plan 28 , and that is also the name of a charity that i started with doron swade , who was the curator of computing at the science museum , and also the person who drove the project to build a difference engine , and our plan is to build it .	其中一個是我們稱之為 「 計劃28 」 的計畫 , 這也是我從doronsveade開始的慈善機構 , 他是科學博物館的電腦策展人 , 也是驅動這個計畫建造出差別引擎的人 , 我們的計劃就是建立它 。
here in south kensington , we will build the analytical engine .	在南肯辛頓 , 我們會建立分析引擎 。
the project has a number of parts to it .	這個計劃有幾個部分 。
one was the scanning of babbage's archive .	其中一個是babbage的檔案 。
that's been done . the second is now the study of all of those plans to determine what to build .	這已經完成了 。 第二個是所有這些計畫的研究 , 決定要建構什麼 。
the third part is a computer simulation of that machine , and the last part is to physically build it at the science museum .	第三部分是那台機器的模擬 , 最後一部分是在科學博物館建造它 。
when it's built , you'll finally be able to understand how a computer works , because rather than having a tiny chip in front of you , you've got to look at this humongous thing and say , " ah , i see the memory operating , i see the cpu operating , i hear it operating . i probably smell it operating . "	當它被建造出來時 , 你終於能夠理解電腦是如何運作的 , 因為在你面前的一個小晶片 , 你必須看這個無聊的物品 , 說: 「 啊 , 我看到記憶運作 , 我聽過它運作 。 我可能聞它在運作 。 」
but in between that we're going to do a simulation .	但在這兩者之間 , 我們要做一個模擬 。
babbage himself wrote , he said , as soon as the analytical engine exists , it will surely guide the future course of science .	babbage自己寫了 , 他說 , 當分析引擎存在時 , 它肯定會引導未來的科學課程 。
of course , he never built it , because he was always fiddling with new plans , but when it did get built , of course , in the 1940s , everything changed .	當然 , 他從來沒有打造它 , 因為他一直在尋找新的計劃 , 但當它真的被建造出來時 , 當然 , 一切都改變了 。
now , i'll just give you a little taste of what it looks like in motion with a video which shows just one part of the cpu mechanism working .	現在 , 我來給各位看一下它在動作中看起來的樣子 , 它顯示了cpu機制運作的一部分 。
so this is just three sets of cogs , and it's going to add . this is the adding mechanism in action , so you imagine this gigantic machine .	這只是三組的齒輪 , 加上它的作用 。 這是加強機制的動作 , 所以你想像一下這個巨大的機器 。
so , give me five years .	所以 , 給我五年 。
before the 2030s happen , we'll have it .	在2030年發生之前 , 我們將會有它 。
thank you very much .	非常謝謝大家
in this imagefilled talk , yann arthusbertrand displays his three most recent projects on humanity and our habitat stunning aerial photographs in his series " the earth from above , " personal interviews from around the globe featured in his web project " 6 billion others , " and his soontobereleased movie , " home , " which documents human impact on the environment through breathtaking video .	在這個影像的演說中 , yannhusbertrand展示了他三個近期的項目 , 關於人類和我們的棲息地 , 在他的系列 「 地球 」 中 , 來自全球各地的個人訪談 , 在他的網站上寫了 「 六十億人 」 , 以及他的 「 即時公開的電影 」 , 記錄了人類對環境的影響 。
art , climate change , environment , film , future , humanity , media , photography	藝術、氣候變遷、環境、未來、人類、媒體、攝影、攝影、攝影 。
yann arthusbertrand captures fragile earth in wideangle	yan'sbertrand捕捉著脆弱的地球 , 位在廣大的角度 , 位於廣大的地球上 。
i have a big impact on the planet to travel here by plane .	我對地球有很大的影響力 , 靠飛機來到這裡旅行 。
i emitted , in the atmosphere , nine tons of co2 ; that is the weight of two elephants .	我在大氣中排放了九噸的二氧化碳 , 這是兩個大象的重量 。
i came here to speak about ecology , and i emitted as much co2 as a frenchman in one year .	我來到這裡 , 談到生態學 , 一年內我就排放了相當多二氧化碳 。
so what do i have to do ?	所以 , 我該怎麼做 ?
i have to kill a frenchman when i come back at home ?	當我回到家時 , 我必須殺死法國人 ?
i have to do my carbon offset in another way , like i do every time .	我得要用另一種方式來抵抗我的碳 , 就像我每次都這樣做 。
in fact my work is to show our impact on our planet .	事實上 , 我的作品是要展示我們對地球的影響 。
i'm going to show you some examples of the last pictures i've done in the last year .	我要給你們看一些我過去一年所拍攝的照片 。
alberta sand oil , a lot of pollution .	亞伯塔石油 , 很多污染 。
you know the problem ; we don't want to believe what we know .	你知道問題 ; 我們不想相信我們所知道的 。
in alberta people work nonstop , 24 hours by seven to extract as much oil as they can .	在亞伯拉塔人工作時 , 24小時 , 7小時 , 盡可能提煉石油 。
we know about the end of oil .	我們知道石油的終點 。
oil sand is not a longterm solution .	石油沙不是長期的解決方案 。
but we use three times more oil than we find every year .	但我們每年用的石油比我們所發現的還要多三倍 。
we don't want to believe what we know .	我們不想相信我們所知道的 。
coral reef in new caledonia .	新卡里尼亞的珊瑚礁 。
100 percent of the coral may be wiped out before 2050 because of global warming .	珊瑚的百分之百可能在2050之前就消失了 , 因為全球暖化 。
and you know how coral are very sensitive to temperature , and are very important for the biodiversity of the sea .	你知道珊瑚對溫度非常敏感 , 對海洋的生物多樣性很重要 。

now there is a new way open between atlantic and pacific .	現在 , 大西洋和太平洋之間有一個新的開放方式 。
the thickness of the arctic decreased more than 40 percent since 1960 .	從1960年起 , 北極的厚度減少了超過40% 。

according to scientists , in 100 years all the mountain glacier will be gone .	根據科學家 , 一百年來 , 所有山上的冰河都會消失 。
glaciers are very important for the life on earth .	冰河對地球上的生命是非常重要的 。
like al gore told you , two billion people live on the water from the glacier of himalaya .	就像高爾說的 , 有二十億人住在喜馬拉雅冰河的水上 。

our life is tied to the wellbeing of our planet .	我們的生命與地球的幸福有關 。

and what binds us together is far greater than what divides us .	把我們結合在一起 , 遠比我們分裂的更大 。
we all share the same need for the earth's gifts the same wish to rise above ourselves , and become better .	我們都一樣對地球的禮物有同樣的需求 , 希望能在我們自己上升 , 變得更好 。
and yet we carry on raising walls to keep us apart .	然而 , 我們還是繼續在提升牆壁 , 讓我們無法分裂 。
today our greatest battle is to protect the natural offerings of our planet .	今天 , 我們最大的戰役就是保護地球的天然資源 。
in less than 50 years we've altered it more thoroughly than in the entire history of mankind .	不到五十年 , 我們徹底地改變它 , 比人類的整個歷史更為徹底 。
half of the world's forests have vanished .	世界上一半的森林都消失了 。
water resources are running low .	水資源正在下降 。
intensive farming is depleting soils .	密集農業正在耗盡土壤 。
our energy sources are not sustainable .	我們的能量來源不是永續的 。
the climate is changing .	氣候正在改變 。
we are endangering ourselves .	我們正在危害我們自己 。
we're only trying to improve our lives .	我們只想改善我們的生活 。
but the wealth gaps are growing wider .	但財富差距越來越廣 。
we haven't yet understood that we're going at a much faster pace than the planet can sustain .	我們還沒料到 , 我們要的速度比地球能維持的更快 。
we know that solutions are available today .	我們知道 , 現今的解決方案是可用的 。

in this accessible talk from tedxboston , richard resnick shows how cheap and fast genome sequencing is about to turn health care upside down .	在這場tedxboston的演講中 , 理查•雷斯尼克提到 , 便宜且快速的基因組定序即將降低健康照護 。
dna , biotech , health care , science , technology	dna、生物科技、健康照護、科學、科技、科技、科技、科技、科技、科技、科技 。
richard resnick: welcome to the genomic revolution	理查•雷尼克:歡迎來到基因革命 。
ladies and gentlemen , i present to you the human genome .	各位先生女士 , 我向各位展示人類基因組 。
chromosome one , top left .	染色體 , 左上方 。
bottom right are the sex chromosomes .	右下角是性染色體 。
women have two copies of that big x chromosome ; men have the x and , of course , that small copy of the y .	女性有兩份大x染色體的複製品 ; 男性有xx , 當然 , 還有y的小複製品 。
sorry boys , but it's just a tiny little thing that makes you different .	抱歉男孩 , 但這只是一件小事 , 讓你有所不同 。
so if you zoom in on this genome , then what you see , of course , is this double helix structure the code of life spelled out with these four biochemical letters , or we call them bases , right: a , c , g and t .	所以如果你放大這個基因組 , 你可以看到 , 雙螺旋結構是生命的編碼 , 用這四個生物化學字母 , 或者我們稱它們為基礎 , 右邊是a、g和t 。
how many are there in the human genome ? three billion .	在人類基因組中有多少 ? 三十億 。
is that a big number ?	這是個大數字嗎 ?
well , everybody can throw around big numbers .	嗯 , 每個人都可以瀏覽大量的數字 。
but in fact , if i were to place one base on each pixel of this 1280 by 800 resolution screen , we would need 3 , 000 screens to take a look at the genome .	但事實上 , 如果我在1280年到800個像素的每一塊像素上放一個基礎 , 我們需要300個螢幕來觀察基因組 。
so it's really quite big .	這真的很大 。
and perhaps because of its size , a group of people all , by the way , with y chromosomes decided they would want to sequence it .	也許是因為它的大小 , 一群人 , 順帶一提 , y染色體決定他們會想要定序 。
and so 15 years , actually , and about four billion dollars later , the genome was sequenced and published .	十五年後 , 大約四十億美金後 , 基因組被定序並發表 。
in 2003 , the final version was published , and they keep working on it .	2003年 , 最後的版本被發表了 , 他們繼續研究它 。
that was all done on a machine that looks like this .	這一切都在機器上完成 , 看起來像這樣 。
it costs about a dollar for each base a very slow way of doing it .	每一塊錢 , 每一塊都要花很慢的路要做 。
well folks , i'm here to tell you that the world has completely changed and none of you know about it .	嗯 , 我來這裡要告訴各位 , 世界已經完全改變 , 你們都不知道 。
so now what we do is we take a genome , we make maybe 50 copies of it , we cut all those copies up into little 50base reads , and then we sequence them , massively parallel .	所以現在我們要做的是把基因組做成50份 , 我們把所有複製品切成五十鹼基的閱讀 , 然後我們將它們進行序列 , 非常平行 。
and then we bring that into software , and we reassemble it and we tell you what the story is .	然後我們把這個軟體帶進軟體裡 , 重新組合 , 告訴你這個故事是什麼 。
and so just to give you a picture of what this looks like , the human genome project: 3 gigabases , right .	所以 , 給大家看一下這個樣子 , 人類基因組計畫:3gbabes , 對 。
one run on one of these machines: 200 gigabases in a week .	一個在其中一個機器上跑:一個禮拜內200gbabas 。
and that 200 is going to change to 600 this summer , and there's no sign of this pace slowing .	今年夏天將改變到六百個 , 沒有這種減速的跡象 。
so the price of a base , to sequence a base , has fallen 100 million times .	所以 , 基地的價格 , 來定序一個基礎 , 已經下降了一億倍 。
that's the equivalent of you filling up your car with gas in 1998 , waiting until 2011 , and now you can drive to jupiter and back twice .	這等同於1998年填滿你車輛的汽油 , 等到2011年 , 現在你可以開車到木星再回來兩次 。
world population , pc placements , the archive of all the medical literature , moore's law , the old way of sequencing , and here's all the new stuff .	世界人口、pc定位、所有醫學文獻、摩爾定律、舊方式定序 , 所有新東西 。
guys , this is a log scale ; you don't typically see lines that go up like that .	各位 , 這是個邏輯尺度 ; 你通常不會看到像這樣的線條 。
so the worldwide capacity to sequence human genomes is something like 50 , 000 to 100 , 000 human genomes this year .	人類基因組測序的能力是今年的五萬到十萬個人類基因組 。
and we know this based on the machines that are being placed .	我們也知道 , 基於被放置的機器 。
this is expected to double , triple or maybe quadruple year over year for the foreseeable future .	這是預期的兩倍、三倍或四倍的未來 。
in fact , there's one lab in particular that represents 20 percent of all that capacity .	事實上 , 特別是有一個實驗室 , 代表所有這些能力的20% 。
it's called the beijing genomics institute .	叫做北京基因學研究所 。
the chinese are absolutely winning this race to the new moon , by the way .	中國人對新的月球來說絕對是贏了 。
what does this mean for medicine ?	這對醫學有什麼意義 ?
so a woman is age 37 .	所以 , 一個女人37歲 。
she presents with stage 2 estrogen receptorpositive breast cancer .	她帶著 「 階段二 」 的雌激素接收腫瘤 。
she is treated with surgery , chemotherapy and radiation .	她接受手術、化療和放射治療 。
two years later , she comes back with stage three c ovarian cancer .	兩年後 , 她得到了第三個卵巢癌 。
unfortunately , treated again with surgery and chemotherapy .	不幸的是 , 再次接受手術和化療治療 。
she comes back three years later at age 42 with more ovarian cancer , more chemotherapy .	三年後 , 她回到了42歲 , 患有更多卵巢癌 , 較多的化療 。
six months later , she comes back with acute myeloid leukemia .	六個月後 , 她帶著急性白血病回來 。
she goes into respiratory failure and dies eight days later .	她走進呼吸道失敗 , 八天後就死了 。
so first , the way in which this woman was treated , in as little as 10 years , will look like bloodletting .	首先 , 這個女人在十年內被治療的方式 , 看起來就像是血液循環一樣 。
and it's because of people like my colleague , rick wilson , at the genome institute at washington university , who decided to take a look at this woman postmortem .	由於像我的同事rickwilson在華盛頓大學的基因研究所 , 他決定去看這位女子的後遺症 。
and he sequenced , he took skin cells , healthy skin , and cancerous bone marrow , and he sequenced the whole genomes of both of them in a couple of weeks , no big deal .	他的基因序列 , 將皮膚細胞、健康的皮膚和癌症骨髓定序 , 幾週內 , 兩者的基因組 , 沒什麼大不了的 。
and then he compared those two genomes in software , and what he found , among other things , was a deletion , a 2 , 000base deletion across three billion bases in a particular gene called tp53 .	接著 , 他比較了軟體中這兩種基因組 , 他發現 , 在其他東西當中 , 是一種刪除 , 兩千個鹼基在一個叫做tp53的基因中 。
if you have this deleterious mutation in this gene , you're 90 percent likely to get cancer in your life .	如果你在這個基因中有這種惡性突變 , 你有90%的可能性會罹患癌症 。
so unfortunately , this doesn't help this woman , but it does have severe , profound if you will , implications to her family .	不幸的是 , 這並不幫助這位女士 , 但這確實有嚴重、深刻的影響她的家人 。
i mean , if they have the same mutation , and they get this genetic test , and they understand it , then they can go and get regular screens , and they can catch cancer early and potentially live a significantly longer life .	我的意思是 , 如果它們有相同的突變 , 它們會得到這個基因測驗 , 它們會了解它 , 並且得到常規的螢幕 , 它們可以在早期發現癌症 , 且可能活得更久 。
let me introduce you now to the beery twins , diagnosed with cerebral palsy at the age of two .	讓我向各位介紹beery雙胞胎 , 在兩歲時 , 被診斷出腦性麻痺症 。
their mom is a very brave woman who didn't believe that the symptoms weren't matching up , and through some heroic efforts and a lot of internet searching , she was able to convince the medical community that , in fact , they had something else .	他們的母親是一位非常勇敢的女性 , 她不相信症狀並不會跟上 , 透過一些英勇的努力和許多網路搜尋 , 她能夠說服醫學界 , 事實上 , 他們還有別的東西 。
what they had was doparesponsive dystonia .	他們有的就是多數的失調症 。
and so they were given ldopa , and their symptoms did improve , but they weren't totally asymptomatic .	所以他們得到了ldopa , 他們的症狀改善了 , 但他們並沒有完全的症狀 。
turns out the gentleman in this picture is a guy named joe beery , who was lucky enough to be the cio of a company called life technologies .	結果是這張照片裡的先生是一位叫jebeery的傢伙 , 他很幸運成為一家叫做 「 生命科技 」 的公司 。
they're one of the two companies that makes these massive whole genome sequencing tools .	它們是兩家公司 , 製造出大量的基因組定序工具的公司之一 。
and so what he did was he got his kids sequenced .	所以他做的是 , 他給了他的孩子定序 。
and what they found was a series of mutations in a gene called spr , which is responsible for producing serotonin , among other things .	他們發現的是一系列的突變 , 一種叫做 「 肝臟 」 的基因 , 它負責生產血清素 , 其它東西 。
so on top of ldopa , they gave these kids a serotonin precursor drug , and they're effectively normal now .	所以 , 在大烏托邦的頂端 , 他們給這些孩子一個血清素前吸毒 , 現在他們是正常的 。
guys , this would never have happened without whole genome sequencing .	各位 , 沒有完整的基因序列 , 這絕對不會發生 。
and at the time this was a few years ago it cost $100 , 000 .	幾年前 , 花了十萬美金 。
today it's $10 , 000 . next year it's $1 , 000 .	今天是一萬美金 , 明年是一千美金 。
the year after it's $100 , give or take a year .	一百元後的一年 , 付出或花一整年 。
that's how fast this is moving .	這就是移動的速度 。
so here's little nick likes batman and squirt guns .	這裡有一些像蝙蝠俠和松鼠的小腿 。
and it turns out nick shows up at the children's hospital with this distended belly like a famine victim .	結果發現尼克出現在兒童醫院 , 帶著這種偏離的肚子 , 就像是饑荒受害者 。
and it's not that he's not eating , it's that when he eats , his intestine basically opens up and feces spill out into his gut .	不是他不吃的 , 而是當他吃東西的時候 , 他的腸子基本上會打開來餵食 , 進到他的腸子裡 。
so a hundred surgeries later , he looks at his mom and says , " mom , please pray for me . i'm in so much pain . "	一百個手術後 , 他看著他的母親 , 說: 「 媽 , 請為我禱告 。 我非常痛苦 。 」
his pediatrician happens to have a background in clinical genetics and he has no idea what's going on , but he says , " let's get this kid's genome sequenced . "	他的小兒科醫師剛好有臨床遺傳學背景 , 他不知道發生了什麼事 , 但他說: 「 讓我們讓這個孩子的基因組定序 。 」
and what they find is a singlepoint mutation in a gene responsible for controlling programmed cell death .	他們發現一個單一的突變 , 由控制細胞死亡的基因負責 。
so the theory is that he's having some immunological reaction to what's going on to the food essentially , and that's a natural reaction , which causes some programmed cell death .	理論是 , 他對食物本質上所發生的免疫反應有一些免疫反應 , 這是天然的反應 , 造成了一些程式化的細胞死亡 。
but the gene that regulates that down is broken .	但法規的基因卻被破壞了 。

and after nine months of grueling recovery , he's now eating steak with a1 sauce .	經過九個月的艱難復原之後 , 他現在在吃史達克 , 吃了一顆醬 。
the prospect of using the genome as a universal diagnostic is upon us today .	把基因組當作一個普遍的診斷 , 正是我們今天所面臨的 。

which is a fantastic story , unless you think about humanity's footprint on the planet and our ability to keep up food production .	這是個很棒的故事 , 除非你考慮到人類對地球的足跡以及我們維持食物生產的能力 。
so it turns out that the very same technology is also being used to grow new lines of corn , wheat , soybean and other crops that are highly tolerant of drought , of flood , of pests and pesticides .	結果發現 , 同樣的技術也被用來種植玉米、小麥、大豆和其他農作物 , 都是高度包容的乾旱、洪水、害蟲和殺蟲劑 。
now look , as long as we continue to increase the population , we're going to have to continue to grow and eat genetically modified foods , and that's the only position that i'll take today .	看 , 只要我們持續增加人口 , 我們就得要持續成長並吃基因改造的食物 , 這就是我今天唯一要採取的立場 。

so , a few years ago , i'm doing my transplant fellowship at stanford .	幾年前 , 我在史丹佛的移植人員 。
i'm in the operating room . we have bob here , who is a volunteer donor .	我在手術室 , 我們有鮑勃 , 他是志願捐贈者 。
we're sending his marrow across the country to save the life of a child with leukemia .	我們把他的骨髓送到全國 , 以拯救白血病孩童的生命 。
so actually how do we harvest this bone marrow ?	所以 , 我們要如何收集這些骨髓 ?
well we have a whole o . r . team , general anesthesia , nurses , and another doctor across from me .	我們有一個全部的o.r.團隊 , 普通麻醉、護士 , 和另一位醫生對我說話 。
bob's on the table , and we take this sort of small needle , you know , not too big .	鮑勃站在桌子上 , 我們拿著這個小針 , 你知道的 , 不是太大 。
and the way we do this is we basically place this through the soft tissue , and kind of punch it into the hard bone , into the tuchus that's a technical term and aspirate about 10 mls of bone marrow out , each time , with a syringe .	基本上 , 我們的做法是把這放在軟組織中 , 把它打進硬骨裡 , 進入管道 , 一個技術的詞 , 每次用針筒挖出十磅的骨髓 。
and hand it off to the nurse . she squirts it into a tin .	然後把它交給護士 。 她將它放進一個薄片裡 。
hands it back to me . and we do that again and again .	把它們交給我 。 我們一次又一次的做這件事 。
about 200 times usually .	通常是兩百次 。
and by the end of this my arm is sore , i've got a callus on my hand , let alone bob , whose rear end looks something more like this , like swiss cheese .	到了我的手臂的尾聲 , 我手上有個叫聲 , 更不用說鮑勃 , 他的屁股看起來像這樣 , 像瑞士起士 。
so i'm thinking , you know , this procedure hasn't changed in about 40 years .	所以我在想 , 大概40年來 , 這種程序並沒有改變 。
and there is probably a better way to do this .	或許還有更好的方法可以做這件事 。
so i thought of a minimally invasive approach , and a new device that we call the marrow miner .	所以我想到一個最低侵入性的方法 , 我們稱之為 「 骨髓礦物 」 。
and the marrow miner , the way it works is shown here .	而骨髓礦工 , 它的運作方式在這裡 。
our standard seethrough patient .	我們的標準透明的病人 。
instead of entering the bone dozens of times , we enter just once , into the front of the hip or the back of the hip .	與其進入骨頭的數十次 , 我們進入了一次 , 進入髖部或背部的前面 。
and we have a flexible , powered catheter with a special wire loop tip that stays inside the crunchy part of the marrow and follows the contours of the hip , as it moves around .	我們有一個彈性、強力的導管 , 帶著一個特殊的電線循環 , 留在骨髓中 , 跟著骨髓的輪廓 , 隨著它移動 。
so it enables you to very rapidly aspirate , or suck out , rich bone marrow very quickly through one hole .	所以它會讓你非常快速地渴望 , 或吸出富人的骨髓 , 非常快地通過一個洞 。
we can do multiple passes through that same entry .	我們可以通過相同的入口進行多次傳遞 。
and , so , very quickly , bob can just get one puncture , local anesthesia , and do this harvest as an outpatient .	所以 , 很快地 , 鮑勃只能用一針針針穿刺 , 當地的麻醉 , 把這個收穫做成耐心 。
so i did a few prototypes . i got a small little grant at stanford .	於是我做了一些原型 。 我在史丹佛做了一個小小的授權 。
and played around with this a little bit .	再玩一下這個 。
and our team members developed this technology .	我們的團隊成員開發了這項技術 。
and eventually we got two large animals , and pig studies .	最後我們得到了兩個大型動物 , 豬研究 。
and we found , to our surprise , that we not only got bone marrow out , but we got 10 times the stem cell activity in the marrow from the marrow miner , compared to the normal device .	我們驚訝地發現 , 我們不只拿出骨髓 , 我們還收到了10倍的幹細胞活動 , 相較於正常的裝置 。
this device was just fda approved in the last year .	這個裝置在去年就被核准了 。
here is a live patient . you can see it following the flexible curves around .	這裡是現場的病人 , 你可以看到它遵循著彈性的曲線 。
there will be two passes here , in the same patient , from the same hole .	同一個病人 , 會在同一個洞的同一個洞裡 。
this was done under local anesthesia , as an outpatient .	這是在本地麻醉的情況下進行的 。
and we got , again , about three to six times more stem cells than the standard approach done on the same patient .	同樣的 , 我們得到的幹細胞 , 比同一個患者的標準來得多3到6倍 。
so why should you care ? bone marrow is a very rich source of adult stem cells .	你為什麼要在乎 ? 骨髓是成人幹細胞非常豐富的來源 。
you all know about embryonic stem cells .	你們都知道胚胎幹細胞 。
they've got great potential but haven't yet entered clinical trials .	他們有很大的潛力 , 但尚未進入臨床試驗 。
adult stem cells are throughout our body , including the bloodforming stem cells in our bone marrow , which we've been using as a form of stemcell therapy for over 40 years .	成人幹細胞遍佈我們的身體 , 包括我們骨髓中血液改造的幹細胞 , 我們已經使用這種幹細胞治療已經超過40年了 。
in the last decade there's been an explosion of use of bone marrow stem cells to treat the patient's other diseases such as heart disease , vascular disease , orthopedics , tissue engineering , even in neurology to treat parkinson's and diabetes .	在過去十年間 , 用骨髓幹細胞來治療病人的其他疾病 , 例如心臟病、血管疾病 , 組織工程 , 甚至神經科全書治療帕金森氏症和糖尿病 。
we've just come out , we're commercializing , this year , generation 2 . 0 of the marrow miner .	今年 , 我們才剛出發 , 我們在商業化 , 今年2.0個骨髓礦工 。
the hope is that this gets more stem cells out , which translates to better outcomes .	希望這能讓更多的幹細胞變得更好 , 讓它轉化成更好的結果 。
it may encourage more people to sign up to be potential livesaving bone marrow donors .	它可能會鼓勵更多人登記 , 成為潛在生命的骨髓捐贈者 。
it may even enable you to bank your own marrow stem cells , when you're younger and healthier , to use in the future should you need it .	它甚至可能讓你能夠銀行你自己的骨髓幹細胞 , 當你年輕、更健康時 , 用在未來 , 你應該需要它 。
and ultimately and here's a picture of our bone marrow transplant survivors , who come together for a reunion each year at stanford .	最後 , 這張是我們骨髓移植的倖存者的照片 , 每年都在史丹佛聚會 。
hopefully this technology will let us have more of these survivors in the future .	希望這項技術能讓我們未來有更多的倖存者 。
physicist and surfer garrett lisi presents a controversial new model of the universe that just maybe answers all the big questions . if nothing else , it's the most beautiful 8dimensional model of elementary particles and forces you've ever seen .	物理學家和衝浪者葛瑞特•萊西提出了一個爭議性的新模型 , 一個可能可以回答所有大問題的宇宙 。 如果什麼都沒有 , 它是最美麗的 「 基本粒子 」 , 和 「 你看過的力 。
physics , science , technology	物理、科學、技術、技術 。
garrett lisi on his theory of everything	在他的理論上 , arretttlisi在他的所有東西的理論上 , 都在他的所有東西的理論中 。
whoa , dude . check out those killer equations . sweet .	哇 ! 老兄 , 看看那些殺手方程式 。
actually , for the next 18 minutes i'm going to do the best i can to describe the beauty of particle physics without equations .	事實上 , 接下來的十八分鐘 , 我要盡我所能描述粒子物理的美好 , 不用方程式來形容 。
it turns out there's a lot we can learn from coral .	結果發現 , 我們可以從珊瑚身上學到很多 。
coral is a very beautiful and unusual animal .	珊瑚是一種非常美麗且不尋常的動物 。
each coral head consists of thousand of individual polyps .	每個珊瑚都包含了一千個個獨立的聚合物 。
these polyps are continually budding and branching into genetically identical neighbors .	這些聚合物不斷地擴散並分成基因相同的鄰居 。
if we imagine this to be a hyperintelligent coral , we can single out an individual and ask him a reasonable question .	如果我們想像這是一個超級智慧的珊瑚 , 我們就能把一個人分離出來 , 並問他一個合理的問題 。
we can ask how exactly he got to be in this particular location compared to his neighbors if it was just chance , or destiny , or what ?	我們可以問他在這個特定的地點和鄰居相比 , 如果只是機會 , 或命運 , 又怎樣 ?
now , after admonishing us for turning the temperature up too high , he would tell us that our question was completely stupid .	現在 , 在我們要求將溫度提高太高之後 , 他會告訴我們 , 我們的問題完全是愚蠢的 。
these corals can be quite kind of mean , you see , and i have surfing scars to prove that .	這些珊瑚可以是相當明確的意思 , 我有衝浪的疤痕來證明它 。
but this polyp would continue and tell us that his neighbors were quite clearly identical copies of him .	但這隻多利普會繼續告訴我們 , 他的鄰居很明顯是同一複製他 。
that he was in all these other locations as well , but experiencing them as separate individuals .	他也身在其他地方 , 但身為不同的個體 , 讓他們體驗到他們 。
for a coral , branching into different copies is the most natural thing in the world .	對珊瑚而言 , 分成不同的複製品是世界上最自然的東西 。
unlike us , a hyperintelligent coral would be uniquely prepared to understand quantum mechanics .	和我們不同 , 超級智慧的珊瑚會是非常獨特的準備來了解量子力學 。
the mathematics of quantum mechanics very accurately describes how our universe works .	量子力學的數學非常精確地描述我們的宇宙是如何運作的 。
and it tells us our reality is continually branching into different possibilities , just like a coral .	它告訴我們 , 我們的現實是不斷地分裂成不同的可能性 , 就像珊瑚一樣 。
it's a weird thing for us humans to wrap our minds around , since we only ever get to experience one possibility .	這對我們人類來說是一件很奇怪的事 , 因為我們只能體驗一個可能性 。
this quantum weirdness was first described by erwin schrödinger and his cat .	這種量子奇怪的最初是由erwinschordinger和他的貓所描述 。
the cat likes this version better .	貓比較喜歡這個版本 。
in this setup , schrödinger is in a box with a radioactive sample that , by the laws of quantum mechanics , branches into a state in which it is radiated and a state in which it is not .	在這個裝置中 , 薛丁格在一個裝有放射性樣本的盒子裡 , 由量子力學的定律 , 分支到一個狀態 , 它是被放射線和狀態的狀態 。
in the branch in which the sample radiates , it sets off a trigger that releases poison and schrödinger is dead .	在這個分支中 , 樣本放射線 , 會造成觸發 , 釋放毒素和薛丁格已死 。
but in the other branch of reality , he remains alive .	但在現實的另一個分支中 , 他仍然活著 。
these realities are experienced separately by each individual .	每一個人都有不同的經歷 。
as far as either can tell , the other one doesn't exist .	無論如何 , 另一種都不存在 。
this seems weird to us , because each of us only experiences an individual existence , and we don't get to see other branches .	這對我們來說很奇怪 , 因為我們每個人都只會經歷個人存在 , 而我們卻看不到其他分支 。
it's as if each of us , like schrödinger here , are a kind of coral branching into different possibilities .	這就好像我們每一個人 , 像薛丁格一樣 , 是一種珊瑚分裂成不同的可能性 。
the mathematics of quantum mechanics tells us this is how the world works at tiny scales .	量子力學的數學告訴我們 , 世界是如何在微小的尺度上運作的 。
it can be summed up in a single sentence: everything that can happen , does .	它可以在單一句話中總結:所有可能發生的一切 。
but this does not mean everything happens .	但這並不意味著一切都發生了 。
the rest of physics is about describing what can happen and what can't .	其餘的物理是描述可能發生什麼事 , 以及什麼是不可行的 。
what physics tells us is that everything comes down to geometry and the interactions of elementary particles .	物理告訴我們 , 所有東西都歸功於幾何和基本粒子的互動 。
and things can happen only if these interactions are perfectly balanced .	只有在這些交互作用完全平衡的情況下 , 情況才會發生 。
now i'll go ahead and describe how we know about these particles , what they are and how this balance works .	現在我要向前描述一下我們對這些粒子的認識 , 它們是什麼 , 以及這個平衡是如何運作的 。
in this machine , a beam of protons and antiprotons are accelerated to near the speed of light and brought together in a collision , producing a burst of pure energy .	在這個機器中 , 一道質子和反物質被加速到接近光速的距離 , 並在碰撞中產生一個純能量的爆炸 。
this energy is immediately converted into a spray of subatomic particles , with detectors and computers used to figure out their properties .	這種能量馬上被轉換成亞原子粒子噴灑 , 用探測儀和電腦來找出它們的特性 。
this enormous machine the large hadron collider at cern in geneva has a circumference of 17 miles and , when it's operating , draws five times as much power as the city of monterey .	這種巨大的機器 , 在日內瓦的大型強子對撞機有17英里的圓形 , 當它在運作時 , 畫了5倍的電力 , 就像蒙特雷市一樣 。
we can't predict specifically what particles will be produced in any individual collision .	我們不能明確地預測哪些粒子會在任何個別碰撞中產生 。
quantum mechanics tells us all possibilities are realized .	量子力學告訴我們所有可能性 。
but physics does tell us what particles can be produced .	但物理學確實告訴我們哪些粒子能產生什麼 。
these particles must have just as much mass and energy as is carried in by the proton and antiproton .	這些粒子必須有相同的質量和能量 , 就像質子和反粒子一樣 。
any particles more massive than this energy limit aren't produced , and remain invisible to us .	任何一個粒子比這個能量限制更大 , 都沒有我們產生 , 對我們來說仍然是看不見的 。
this is why this new particle accelerator is so exciting .	這就是為什麼這個新粒子加速器這麼令人興奮 。
it's going to push this energy limit seven times beyond what's ever been done before , so we're going to get to see some new particles very soon .	它將在過去七倍以外的能源限制 , 我們很快就會看到一些新粒子 。
but before talking about what we might see , let me describe the particles we already know of .	但在談談我們可能看到的之前 , 讓我描述一下我們已知的粒子 。
there's a whole zoo of subatomic particles .	有一大堆亞原子粒子 。
most of us are familiar with electrons .	我們大部分人都熟悉電子 。
a lot of people in this room make a good living pushing them around .	在這間房間裡 , 很多人會做個好的活生生生生的動力 。
but the electron also has a neutral partner called the neutrino , with no electric charge and a very tiny mass .	但電子也有一個中立的夥伴 , 叫做中子 , 沒有電荷和一個非常小的質量 。
in contrast , the upanddown quarks have very large masses , and combine in threes to make the protons and neutrons inside atoms .	相較之下 , 由上而下的夸克有很大的質量 , 將三者結合 , 讓質子和中子在原子裡面 。
all of these matter particles come in left and righthanded varieties , and have antiparticle partners that carry opposite charges .	所有這些物質粒子都出現在左邊 , 和右手邊的各式各樣 , 有反粒子伴侶 , 攜帶相反載荷 。
these familiar particles also have less familiar second and third generations , which have the same charges as the first but have much higher masses .	這些熟悉的粒子也比較不熟悉的第二代和第三代 , 和第一代相同的載荷 , 但質量較高 。
these matter particles all interact with the various force particles .	這些物質粒子都與不同的力粒子互動 。
the electromagnetic force interacts with electrically charged matter via particles called photons .	電磁力的作用力通過粒子稱為光子的電導電粒子
there is also a very weak force called , rather unimaginatively , the weak force , that interacts only with lefthanded matter .	還有一種非常弱的力量 , 叫做 「 不可思議的弱力 」 , 只和左撇子有所互動 。
the strong force acts between quarks which carry a different kind of charge , called color charge , and come in three different varieties: red , green and blue .	夸克之間的強力作用 , 帶有不同的載荷 , 叫做顏色載荷 , 來到三種不同的品種:紅、綠和藍 。
you can blame murray gellmann for these names they're his fault .	你可以怪murraygellmann的名字 , 他們是他的錯 。
finally , there's the force of gravity , which interacts with matter via its mass and spin .	最後 , 有重力 , 透過質量和旋轉來互動 。
the most important thing to understand here is that there's a different kind of charge associated with each of these forces .	最重要的是 , 這裡有一種不同的載荷 , 和這些力有關 。
these four different forces interact with matter according to the corresponding charges that each particle has .	這四種不同的力量 , 根據各個粒子所擁有的負責荷來與物質互動 。
a particle that hasn't been seen yet , but we're pretty sure exists , is the higgs particle , which gives masses to all these other particles .	目前還沒看過的粒子 , 但我們非常確定存在 , 是希格斯粒子 , 它給了所有粒子的質量 。
the main purpose of the large hadron collider is to see this higgs particle , and we're almost certain it will .	大型強子對撞機的主要目的是看到這個希格斯粒子 , 我們幾乎肯定它會 。
but the greatest mystery is what else we might see .	但最大的謎團是我們所見到的 。
and i'm going to show you one beautiful possibility towards the end of this talk .	接下來我要給大家看一個美麗的可能性 , 讓大家看看這場演說的尾聲 。
now , if we count up all these different particles using their various spins and charges , there are 226 .	現在 , 如果我們用不同的旋轉和載荷來計算這些不同的粒子 , 就會有226個 。
that's a lot of particles to keep track of .	要追蹤很多粒子 。
and it seems strange that nature would have so many elementary particles .	大自然有這麼多基本粒子 , 似乎很奇怪 。
but if we plot them out according to their charges , some beautiful patterns emerge .	但如果我們根據他們的指控來繪製它們 , 有些美麗的圖案就會浮現出來 。
the most familiar charge is electric charge .	最熟悉的電荷是電荷 。
electrons have an electric charge , a negative one , and quarks have electric charges in thirds .	電子有電荷 , 負電 , 夸克有三分之一的電荷 。
so when two up quarks and a down quark are combined to make a proton , it has a total electric charge of plus one .	所以當兩個高夸克和一個下夸克結合成一個質子 , 總電荷加1 。
these particles also have antiparticles , which have opposite charges .	這些粒子也有反粒子 , 有相反的載荷 。
now , it turns out the electric charge is actually a combination of two other charges: hypercharge and weak charge .	結果發現 , 電荷其實是兩種載荷的組合:超荷和弱荷 。
if we spread out the hypercharge and weak charge and plot the charges of particles in this twodimensional charge space , the electric charge is where these particles sit along the vertical direction .	如果我們把超連結和弱載荷分散出來 , 並在這個二維載荷空間中畫出粒子的載荷 , 電荷就是這些粒子在垂直方向的位置 。
the electromagnetic and weak forces interact with matter according to their hypercharge and weak charge , which make this pattern .	電磁力和弱力會根據它們的超連結和弱載荷 , 產生這種模式 。
this is called the unified electroweak model , and it was put together back in 1967 .	這叫做 「 統一的電擊模型 」 , 它在1967年被組合起來 。
the reason most of us are only familiar with electric charge and not both of these is because of the higgs particle .	我們之所以熟悉電荷 , 是因為希格斯粒子 。
the higgs , over here on the left , has a large mass and breaks the symmetry of this electroweak pattern .	左邊的是希格斯 , 有一個很大的質量 , 打破了這個直立模式的對稱性 。
it makes the weak force very weak by giving the weak particles a large mass .	它會讓弱力非常弱 , 讓微小的粒子成為一個大質量 。
since this massive higgs sits along the horizontal direction in this diagram , the photons of electromagnetism remain massless and interact with electric charge along the vertical direction in this charge space .	自從這個巨大的希格斯位在這個圖形中 , 電磁的光子仍然是無質量的 , 與電荷在這個載荷空間的垂直方向相互作用 。
so the electromagnetic and weak forces are described by this pattern of particle charges in twodimensional space .	所以電磁力和弱力被這種二維空間的粒子載荷所描述 。
we can include the strong force by spreading out its two charge directions and plotting the charges of the force particles in quarks along these directions .	我們能把強力推出兩個載荷方向 , 將這些粒子的載荷分佈在這些方向 。
the charges of all known particles can be plotted in a fourdimensional charge space , and projected down to two dimensions like this so we can see them .	所有已知粒子的載荷可以在四維載荷空間中繪製 , 投射到像這樣的二維空間 , 這樣我們就能看見它們 。
whenever particles interact , nature keeps things in a perfect balance along all four of these charge directions .	每當粒子相互作用時 , 大自然就會讓物體在四個載荷方向都保持完美的平衡 。
if a particle and an antiparticle collide , it creates a burst of energy and a total charge of zero in all four charge directions .	如果粒子和反粒子相撞 , 它會產生能量爆裂 , 並且在四個載荷方向中總收取0 。
at this point , anything can be created as long as it has the same energy and maintains a total charge of zero .	在這個時點 , 任何東西都可以產生 , 只要它有相同的能量 , 維持一個總量的零載荷 。
for example , this weak force particle and its antiparticle can be created in a collision .	例如 , 這種弱力粒子和它的反粒子可以在碰撞中產生 。
in further interactions , the charges must always balance .	在更進一步的互動中 , 載荷一定是平衡的 。
one of the weak particles could decay into an electron and an antineutrino , and these three still add to zero total charge .	其中一個微弱的粒子可以腐化成電子和一個反中子 , 這三種仍然加上零載荷 。
nature always keeps a perfect balance .	大自然總是保持完美的平衡 。
so these patterns of charges are not just pretty .	所以這些載荷的模式並不很漂亮 。
they tell us what interactions are allowed to happen .	他們告訴我們 , 互動是怎樣發生的 。
and we can rotate this charge space in four dimensions to get a better look at the strong interaction , which has this nice hexagonal symmetry .	我們可以在四度空間中旋轉載荷空間 , 讓它更好地看出強度的互動 , 這對稱性很棒 。
in a strong interaction , a strong force particle , such as this one , interacts with a colored quark , such as this green one , to give a quark with a different color charge this red one .	在強力的互動中 , 強力粒子 , 例如這個 , 與有色的夸克互動 , 例如這個綠色的方塊 , 給一個夸克一個不同的顏色負荷這個紅色的粒子 。
and strong interactions are happening millions of times each second in every atom of our bodies , holding the atomic nuclei together .	強烈的互動每秒鐘發生數百萬次 , 在我們身體的每個原子中 , 將原子核結合在一起 。
but these four charges corresponding to three forces are not the end of the story .	但這四個載荷對應三種力量並不是故事的終點 。
we can also include two more charges corresponding to the gravitational force .	我們還可以再加上兩個載荷來對應重力力 。
when we include these , each matter particle has two different spin charges , spinup and spindown .	包含這些 , 每個粒子都有兩個不同的旋轉載荷 , 旋轉和旋轉 。
so they all split , and give a nice pattern in sixdimensional charge space .	所以它們都分裂了 , 在六度載荷空間中 , 給出一個好的圖案 。
we can rotate this pattern in six dimensions , and see that it's quite pretty .	我們可以在六度空間中旋轉這個模式 , 看看它是很漂亮的 。
right now , this pattern matches our best current knowledge of how nature is built at the tiny scales of these elementary particles .	現在 , 這種模式符合我們目前最好的知識 , 了解大自然是如何在這些基本粒子的小尺度上建構出來的 。
this is what we know for certain .	這就是我們所知道的 。
some of these particles are at the very limit of what we've been able to reach with experiments .	有些粒子是非常極限的 , 是我們能夠達到的實驗 。
from this pattern , we already know the particle physics of these tiny scales . the way the universe works with these tiny scales is very beautiful .	從這個圖案中 , 我們已經知道這些微小的尺度的粒子物理 。 宇宙與這些微小的尺度是非常漂亮的 。
but now i'm going to discuss some new and old ideas about things we don't know yet .	但現在我要討論一些我們還不知道的新想法 。
we want to expand this pattern using mathematics alone , and see if we can get our hands on the whole enchilada .	我們只想用數學來拓展這個模式 , 看看我們能不能掌握整個enchilada的手 。
we want to find all the particles and forces that make a complete picture of our universe .	我們想找到所有組成宇宙的粒子和力 。
and we want to use this picture to predict new particles that we'll see when experiments reach higher energies .	我們希望用這張照片來預測新粒子當實驗能達到更高的能量 。
so there's an old idea in particle physics that this known pattern of charges , which is not very symmetric , could emerge from a more perfect pattern that gets broken similar to how the higgs particle breaks the electroweak pattern to give electromagnetism .	在粒子物理學中有一個古老的想法 , 這種已知的載荷模式 , 不對稱 , 可以從一個更完美的模式中浮現 , 讓希格斯粒子斷裂 , 讓電磁性產生電磁性 。
in order to do this , we need to introduce new forces with new charge directions .	為了做到這一點 , 我們需要用新的載荷方向來引導新力量 。
when we introduce a new direction , we get to guess what charges the particles have along this direction , and then we can rotate it in with the others .	當我們引進一個新的方向 , 我們就能猜測這個方向的粒子載荷 , 然後我們可以和其他的粒子旋轉 。
if we guess wisely , we can construct the standard charges in six charge dimensions as a broken symmetry of this more perfect pattern in seven charge dimensions .	如果我們有智慧地猜測 , 我們可以在六度載荷中建立標準載荷 , 作為一個破碎的對稱 , 在七度載荷維度中 , 建立一個更完美的模式 。
this particular choice corresponds to a grand unified theory introduced by pati and salam in 1973 .	在1973年 , 這種特殊的選擇對應了一個大統一理論 , 由pati和salam提出 。
when we look at this new unified pattern , we can see a couple of gaps where particles seem to be missing .	當我們看這個新的統一模式 , 我們可以看到兩個空隙 , 粒子似乎缺少了 。
this is the way theories of unification work .	這是統一理論的運作方式 。
a physicist looks for larger , more symmetric patterns that include the established pattern as a subset .	物理學家會尋找更大、更對稱的圖案 , 把已有的圖案包含成子 。
the larger pattern allows us to predict the existence of particles that have never been seen .	更大的模式讓我們能夠預測從未見過的粒子存在 。
this unification model predicts the existence of these two new force particles , which should act a lot like the weak force , only weaker .	這個統一的模型預測了這兩個新力粒子的存在 , 應該要像弱力一樣 , 只會變弱 。
now we can rotate this set of charges in seven dimensions and consider an odd fact about the matter particles: the second and third generations of matter have exactly the same charges in sixdimensional charge space as the first generation .	我們現在可以在七度空間中旋轉載荷 , 考慮到物質粒子的奇怪事實:第二代和第三代物質在六度載荷空間中有完全相同的載荷空間 。
these particles are not uniquely identified by their six charges .	這些粒子沒有獨特辨識出它們的六載荷 。
they sit on top of one another in the standard charge space .	他們坐在標準載荷空間的另一端 。
however , if we work in eightdimensional charge space , then we can assign unique new charges to each particle .	然而 , 如果我們在八度載荷空間中工作 , 那麼我們就能將獨特的新載荷給每個粒子 。
then we can spin these in eight dimensions , and see what the whole pattern looks like .	然後我們在八度空間內旋轉 , 看看整個圖案看起來是怎樣的 。
here we can see the second and third generations of matter now related to the first generation by a symmetry called " triality . "	這裡我們可以看到第二代和第三代物質的關聯 , 由一種稱為 「 試驗 」 的對稱性 。
this particular pattern of charges in eight dimensions is actually part of the most beautiful geometric structure in mathematics .	這種八度的載荷模式 , 其實是數學中最美麗的幾何結構之一 。
it's a pattern of the largest exceptional lie group , e8 .	這是最大例外的謊言團體 , e8 。
this lie group is a smooth , curved shape with 248 dimensions .	這個謊言團體是平滑的曲線形狀 , 長達248度 。
each point in this pattern corresponds to a symmetry of this very complex and beautiful shape .	在這個圖案中 , 每一點都對應著這個非常複雜且美麗的形狀 。
one small part of this e8 shape can be used to describe the curved spacetime of einstein's general relativity , explaining gravity .	這個e8形狀的一小部分可以用來描述愛因斯坦廣義相對論的曲線 , 解釋重力 。
together with quantum mechanics , the geometry of this shape could describe everything about how the universe works at the tiniest scales .	用量子力學 , 這個形狀的幾何形狀可以描述宇宙如何在最小的尺度上運作的一切 。
the pattern of this shape living in eightdimensional charge space is exquisitely beautiful , and it summarizes thousands of possible interactions between these elementary particles , each of which is just a facet of this complicated shape .	這種形狀的八度載荷空間是非常美麗的 , 它總結了數以千計的基本粒子之間的相互作用 , 每一種都只是面對這種複雜的形狀 。
as we spin it , we can see many of the other intricate patterns contained in this one .	當我們旋轉時 , 我們可以看到許多其他複雜的圖案 , 包含在這個圖案中 。
and with a particular rotation , we can look down through this pattern in eight dimensions along a symmetry axis and see all the particles at once .	通過一個特定的旋轉 , 我們可以從八度的角度看下去 , 透過對稱軸 , 同時看到所有粒子 。
it's a very beautiful object , and as with any unification , we can see some holes where new particles are required by this pattern .	它是一個非常美麗的物品 , 就像任何統一的一樣 , 我們可以看到一些洞 , 在這個圖案所需要的新粒子 。
there are 20 gaps where new particles should be , two of which have been filled by the patisalam particles .	新粒子應該有20個缺口 , 其中兩個是帕帕拉斯山粒子填滿的 。
from their location in this pattern , we know that these new particles should be scalar fields like the higgs particle , but have color charge and interact with the strong force .	從這些圖案的位置 , 我們知道這些新粒子應該是像希格斯粒子的尺度 , 但有顏色負荷和強力的作用 。
filling in these new particles completes this pattern , giving us the full e8 .	填充這些新粒子 , 完成了這個圖案 , 給我們全部的e8 。
this e8 pattern has very deep mathematical roots .	這個e8的圖案有非常深的數學根源 。
it's considered by many to be the most beautiful structure in mathematics .	它被很多人認為是數學中最美麗的結構 。
it's a fantastic prospect that this object of great mathematical beauty could describe the truth of particle interactions at the smallest scales imaginable .	這個偉大的數學美的物體可以描述粒子互動的真相 , 最小的想像力是可想像的 。
and this idea that nature is described by mathematics is not at all new .	這種說法 , 大自然是用數學來描述的 , 並非全新的 。
in 1623 , galileo wrote this: " nature's grand book , which stands continually open to our gaze , is written in the language of mathematics .	1623年 , 伽利略寫了這個: 「 大自然的大書 , 一直對我們的眼神開放 , 寫在數學的語言中 。
its characters are triangles , circles and other geometrical figures , without which it is humanly impossible to understand a single word of it ; without these , one is wandering around in a dark labyrinth . "	它的角色是三角形、圓形和其他幾何圖形 , 沒有它是不可能理解單一個字 ; 若沒有這些 , 就會在黑暗的迷宮中四處遊走 。 」
i believe this to be true , and i've tried to follow galileo's guidance in describing the mathematics of particle physics using only triangles , circles and other geometrical figures .	我相信這是真的 , 我試著遵循伽利略的指引 , 用三角形、圓形和其他幾何形狀來描述粒子物理的數學 。
of course , when other physicists and i actually work on this stuff , the mathematics can resemble a dark labyrinth .	當然 , 當其他物理學家和我真的在做這些東西時 , 數學可以是黑暗的迷宮 。
but it's reassuring that at the heart of this mathematics is pure , beautiful geometry .	但 , 要確保數學的核心是純粹、美麗的幾何學 。
joined with quantum mechanics , this mathematics describes our universe as a growing e8 coral , with particles interacting at every location in all possible ways according to a beautiful pattern .	加入量子力學 , 這種數學描述了我們的宇宙 , 作為一個成長中的e8珊瑚 , 粒子在每個位置都互動 , 根據一個美麗的圖案 。
and as more of the pattern comes into view using new machines like the large hadron collider , we may be able to see whether nature uses this e8 pattern or a different one .	隨著越來越多的模式使用大型強子對撞機的新機器 , 我們可能會看到大自然是否使用e8圖案或不同的圖案 。
this process of discovery is a wonderful adventure to be involved in .	這項發現的過程是一段很棒的冒險旅程 。
if the lhc finds particles that fit this e8 pattern , that will be very , very cool .	如果lhc找到適合e8圖案的粒子 , 那會非常非常的酷 。
if the lhc finds new particles , but they don't fit this pattern well , that will be very interesting , but bad for this e8 theory .	如果lhc找到新的粒子 , 但它們並不符合這個模式 , 那對e8理論來說是很有意思的 , 但對這個e8理論來說卻是不好的 。
and , of course , bad for me personally .	當然 , 對我個人來說 , 不好 。
now how bad would that be ?	那會有多糟 ?
well , pretty bad .	嗯 , 非常糟糕 。
but predicting how nature works is a very risky game .	但預測大自然是如何運作的 , 是個非常危險的遊戲 。
this theory and others like it are long shots .	這個理論和其他類似的理論都很長 。
one does a lot of hard work knowing that most of these ideas probably won't end up being true about nature .	一個人做了很多艱難的工作 , 知道大部分這些想法 , 最終不會是大自然的真理 。
that's what doing theoretical physics is like: there are a lot of wipeouts .	理論物理就是這樣:有很多野生動物 。
in this regard , new physics theories are a lot like startup companies .	在這方面 , 新的物理理論就像新創公司一樣 。
as with any large investment , it can be emotionally difficult to abandon a line of research when it isn't working out .	隨著任何大型投資 , 情緒上就很難放棄一系列的研究 。
but in science , if something isn't working , you have to toss it out and try something else .	但在科學上 , 如果沒有用 , 你就得要去嘗試其他東西 。
now , the only way to maintain sanity and achieve happiness in the midst of this uncertainty is to keep balance and perspective in life .	唯一能維持理智和成就幸福的方法 , 就是保持生活的平衡和觀點 。
i've tried the best i can to live a balanced life .	我盡我所能地嘗試過平衡生活 。
i try to balance my life equally between physics , love and surfing my own three charge directions .	我試著平衡我的人生在物理之間 , 愛和衝浪我自己的三個載荷方向 。
this way , even if the physics i work on comes to nothing , i still know i've lived a good life .	這樣的方式 , 即使我工作的物理都沒有 , 我仍然知道我過著好的生活 。
and i try to live in beautiful places .	我試著生活在美麗的地方 。
for most of the past ten years i've lived on the island of maui , a very beautiful place .	在過去的十年裡 , 我住在馬伊島的大部分時間 , 是一個非常美麗的地方 。
now it's one of the greatest mysteries in the universe to my parents how i managed to survive all that time without engaging in anything resembling fulltime employment .	現在它是宇宙中最偉大的謎團之一 , 是我父母一直以來都無法全職投入任何全職員工 。
i'm going to let you in on that secret .	我會讓你們知道這個秘密
this was a view from my home office on maui .	這是我家在maui的家庭辦公室的景象 。
and you may have noticed that these beautiful views are similar , but in slightly different places .	你可能已經注意到這些美麗的景觀是相似的 , 但在不同的地方 。
that's because this used to be my home and office on maui .	那是因為這曾經是我在毛伊的家和辦公室 。
i've chosen a very unusual life .	我選擇了非常不尋常的人生 。
but not worrying about rent allowed me to spend my time doing what i love .	但不用擔心租金 , 讓我能花時間做我喜愛的事 。
living a nomadic existence has been hard at times , but it's allowed me to live in beautiful places and keep a balance in my life that i've been happy with .	有時 , 居住遊牧的存在很艱難 , 但它讓我能住在美麗的地方 , 保持平衡 , 在我人生中我一直都很快樂 。
it allows me to spend a lot of my time hanging out with hyperintelligent coral .	它允許我花很多時間和超級聰明的珊瑚在一起 。
but i also greatly enjoy the company of hyperintelligent people .	但我也很享受超級聰明人的公司 。
so i'm very happy to have been invited here to ted .	所以我很高興被邀請來ted 。
chris anderson: i probably understood two percent of that , but i still absolutely loved it . so i'm going to sound dumb .	克里斯•安德森:我大概懂了百分之二 , 但我仍然很愛它 。 所以我會聽起來很蠢 。
your theory of everything garrett lisi: i'm used to coral .	你的萬物理論:我習慣珊瑚 。
ca: that's right . the reason it's got a few people at least excited is because , if you're right , it brings gravity and quantum theory together .	克:沒錯 , 原因是 , 至少有幾個人感到興奮 , 因為如果你是對的 , 它會把重力和量子理論結合在一起 。
so are you saying that we should think of the universe , at its heart that the smallest things that there are , are somehow an e8 object of possibility ?	所以 , 你是說 , 我們應該考慮宇宙 , 在它的心中 , 最小的東西 , 可能是e8的物體嗎 ?
i mean , is there a scale to it , at the smallest scale , or . . . ?	我的意思是 , 在最小的尺度上 , 有沒有一個比例 , 還是......
gl: well , right now the pattern i showed you that corresponds to what we know about elementary particle physics that already corresponds to a very beautiful shape .	格林:現在 , 我給你們看的模式是 , 與我們所知的基本粒子物理有關 , 已經對應到一個非常漂亮的形狀 。
and that's the one that i said we knew for certain .	那就是我所說的我們知道的 。
and that shape has remarkable similarities and the way it fits into this e8 pattern could be the rest of the picture .	這種形狀具有驚人的相似性 , 和它適合這個e8的圖案 , 可能是圖片的其他部分 。
and these patterns of points that i've shown for you actually represent symmetries of this highdimensional object that would be warping and moving and dancing over the space time that we experience .	我向各位展示的這些圖案 , 其實是這種高維物體的對稱性 , 會在我們體驗的時空中扭曲、移動、跳舞 。
and that would be what explains all these elementary particles that we see .	那就是解釋我們所看到的這些基本粒子 。
ca: but a string theorist , as i understand it , explains electrons in terms of much smaller strings vibrating i know you don't like string theory vibrating inside it .	克:但弦理論家 , 如我所知 , 它解釋了電子 , 以更小的弦振動我知道你不喜歡弦理論震動它 。
how should we think of an electron in relation to e8 ?	我們該如何看待e8的電子呢 ?
gl: no , it would be one of the symmetries of this e8 shape .	蓋瑞:不 , 它會是e8形狀的對稱性之一 。
so what's happening is , as the shape is moving over spacetime , it's twisting . and the direction it's twisting as it moves is what particle we see . so it would be ca: the size of the e8 shape , how does that relate to the electron ?	所以 , 當這個形狀在時空移動時 , 它會扭曲 。 當它移動時 , 它的方向是我們看到的粒子 。 所以 , 克:e8形狀的大小 , 和電子的關係如何 ?
i kind of feel like i need that for my picture .	我覺得我需要這張照片 。
is it bigger ? is it smaller ?	它會變大嗎 ? 它比較小嗎 ?
gl: well , as far as we know electrons are point particles , so this would be going down to the smallest possible scales .	比爾:嗯 , 目前我們所知的電子是點粒子 , 所以這會降到最小的可能性 。
so the way these things are explained in quantum field theory is , all possibilities are expanding and developing at once .	所以這些東西在量子場理論中被解釋的方式是 , 所有可能性的同時也在擴張和發展中 。
and this is why i use the analogy to coral .	這就是為什麼我會用珊瑚的類比 。
and in this way , the way that e8 comes in is it will be as a shape that's attached at each point in spacetime .	以這種方式來看 , e8會出現的方式 , 就是它的形狀在時空的每一點附著 。
and , as i said , the way the shape twists the directional along which way the shape is twisting as it moves over this curved surface is what the elementary particles are , themselves .	如我所說的 , 形狀的扭曲方向 , 形狀在曲線的表面上移動 , 正是基本粒子本身 。
so through quantum field theory , they manifest themselves as points and interact that way .	所以 , 透過量子場理論 , 它們將自己呈現為點 , 以這種方式互動 。
i don't know if i'll be able to make this any clearer .	我不知道我是否能讓它更清楚 。
ca: it doesn't really matter .	克:這並不重要 。
it's evoking a kind of sense of wonder , and i certainly want to understand more of this .	它在喚起一種奇妙的感覺 , 我當然想了解更多 。
but thank you so much for coming . that was absolutely fascinating .	但 , 非常謝謝你來 。 這絕對是令人著迷的 。
the legendary chimpanzee researcher jane goodall talks about tacare and her other community projects , which help people in booming african towns live sidebyside with threatened animals .	傳奇的黑猩猩研究者珍.古德爾談到坦克和她的其他社區計畫 , 協助非洲城鎮居住在邊緣 , 威脅動物 。
africa , animals , biodiversity , environment , global issues , pollution , primates , science	非洲、動物、生物多樣性、環境、全球性問題、污染、靈長類、科學、科學等問題 。
jane goodall helps humans and animals live together	珍古德幫助人類和動物一起生活
good afternoon , good evening , whatever .	午安 , 晚安 , 等等 。
we can go , jambo , guten abend , bonsoir , but we can also ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh .	我們可以去 , 傑博 , 吉他 , 波諾 , 但我們也能──喔 , 哦 , 哦 , 哦 , 哦 , 哦 , 哦 , 哦 , 喔 , ~ 哦 , 哦 , 哦 , ~ 哦 , 哦 。
that is the call that chimpanzees make before they go to sleep in the evening .	這是黑猩猩在晚上入睡前的電話 。
you hear it going from one side of the valley to the other , from one group of nests to the next .	從山谷的一邊到另一邊 , 從一組的巢穴到下一個 。
and i want to pick up with my talk this evening from where zeray left off yesterday .	昨天晚上 , 我想從昨天zeray留下的位置來談談我的演講 。
he was talking about this amazing , threeyearold australopithecine child , selam .	他談到這個驚人、三歲的澳大利亞小孩 , 塞拉姆 。
and we've also been hearing about the history , the family tree , of mankind through dna genetic profiling .	我們也聽過歷史、家庭樹、人類透過dna的利潤來獲取基因 。
and it was a paleontologist , the late louis leakey , who actually set me on the path for studying chimpanzees .	這位是古生物學家 , 最近的路易斯•李克 , 他讓我踏上研究黑猩猩的路上 。
and it was pretty extraordinary , way back then .	那時候很不可思議 。
it's kind of commonplace now , but his argument was because he'd been searching for the fossilized remains of early humans in africa .	現在有點普遍 , 但他的論點是因為他一直在尋找非洲早期人類的化石遺骸 。
and you can tell an awful lot about what those beings looked like from the fossils , from the shape of the muscle attachments , something about the way they lived from the various artifacts found with them .	你可以從化石的形狀來分辨出那些人的樣子 , 從肌肉附著的形狀 , 和他們生活的方式不同 。
but what about how they behaved ? that's what he wanted to know .	但他們怎麼做呢 ? 這是他想要知道的 。
and of course , behavior doesn't fossilize .	當然 , 行為並不會化石 。
he argued and it's now a fairly common theory that if we found behavior patterns similar or the same in our closest living relatives , the great apes , and humans today , then maybe those behaviors were present in the apelike , humanlike ancestor some seven million years ago .	他主張和現在是一個相當常見的理論 , 如果我們在近親的壽命中找到類似或相同的行為模式 , 人類 , 也許這些行為在七百萬年前出現 , 像是人類的祖先 。
and therefore , perhaps we had brought those characteristics with us from that ancient , ancient past .	因此 , 也許我們從古老、古老的過去帶給我們這些特質 。
well , if you look in textbooks today that deal with human evolution , you very often find people speculating about how early humans may have behaved , based on the behavior of chimpanzees .	嗯 , 假如你現在在教科書裡 , 處理人類進化 , 你經常會發現人們推測早期人類的行為 , 根據黑猩猩的行為 。
they are more like us than any other living creature , and we've heard about that during this ted conference .	它們比任何其他生物更像我們 , 在ted會議中 , 我們也聽過這種說法 。
so it remains for me to comment on the ways in which chimpanzees are so like us , in certain aspects of their behavior .	所以 , 我一直在評論黑猩猩和我們一樣的行為 。 在某些方面 , 黑猩猩和我們是如此相似的 。
every chimpanzee has his or her own personality .	每隻黑猩猩都有自己的個性 。
of course , i gave them names . they can live to be 60 years or more , although we think most of them probably don't make it to 60 in the wild .	當然 , 我會給他們名字 。 他們可以活到60年或更多 , 雖然我們認為大部分的人可能不會在野外生存 。
mr . wurzel . the female has her first baby when she's 11 or 12 .	沃茲先生 , 雌性最早的寶寶在她11或12歲時 。
thereafter , she has one baby only every five or six years , a long period of childhood dependency when the child is nursing , sleeping with the mother at night , and riding on her back .	在那裡 , 她每五到六年就有一個嬰兒 , 一個長期的童年依賴 , 當孩子在生育時 , 晚上和母親一起睡覺 , 騎著她的背 。
and we believe that this long period of childhood is important for chimpanzees , just as it is for us , in relation to learning .	我們相信這段長期的童年期對黑猩猩來說很重要 , 就像對我們而言 , 與學習有關 。
as the brain becomes ever more complex during evolution in different forms of animals , so we find that learning plays an ever more important role in an individual's life history .	隨著大腦在不同形式的動物進化過程中變得更複雜 , 所以我們發現學習在個人的歷史中扮演著更重要的角色 。
and young chimpanzees spend a lot of time watching what their elders do .	年輕的黑猩猩花了很多時間觀察牠們的長老們做了什麼 。
we know now that they're capable of imitating behaviors that they see .	我們現在知道它們能夠模仿它們所看到的行為 。
and we believe that it's in this way that the different toolusing behaviors that have now been seen in all the different chimpanzee populations studied in africa how these are passed from one generation to the next , through observation , imitation and practice , so that we can describe these toolusing behaviors as primitive culture .	我們相信 , 以這種方式 , 這種不同的工具行為 , 如今在非洲各地的黑猩猩族群都在研究這些世代 , 從一個世代到下一代 , 透過觀察、模仿和練習 , 我們就能把這些工具行為描述成原始文化 。
chimpanzees don't have a spoken language . we've talked about that .	黑猩猩沒有口語 , 我們已經談過了 。
they do have a very rich repertoire of postures and gestures , many of which are similar , or even identical , to ours and formed in the same context . greeting chimpanzees embracing .	它們的確有著非常豐富的姿勢和姿勢 , 當中有許多相似 , 甚至相同 , 形成同一個情境 。 希臘黑猩會擁抱擁抱 。
they also kiss , hold hands , pat one another on the back .	他們也親吻、握手、拍下彼此的背 。
and they swagger and they throw rocks .	然後他們搖動 , 扔石頭 。
in chimpanzee society , we find many , many examples of compassion , precursors to love and true altruism .	在黑猩猩社會中 , 我們發現許多關於同情心的例子 , 前往愛和真正的利他主義 。
unfortunately , they , like us , have a dark side to their nature .	不幸的是 , 他們和我們一樣 , 有一面黑暗的天性 。
they're capable of extreme brutality , even a kind of primitive war .	他們有能力極端殘暴 , 甚至是一種原始的戰爭 。
and these really aggressive behaviors , for the most part , are directed against individuals of the neighboring social group .	而這些非常具侵略性的行為 , 大部分的原因是對抗鄰近社會群體的個體 。
they are very territorially aggressive .	它們非常的具攻擊性 。
chimpanzees , i believe , more than any other living creature , have helped us to understand that , after all , there is no sharp line between humans and the rest of the animal kingdom .	我相信 , 比起任何其他生物 , 已經協助我們了解 , 畢竟 , 人類和其他動物王國之間沒有尖銳的線 。
it's a very blurry line , and it's getting more blurry all the time as we make even more observations .	這是一條非常模糊的線 , 每當我們做更多的觀察時 , 它就會變得更模糊 。
the study that i began in 1960 is still continuing to this day .	我1960年開始的研究仍持續著今日 。
and these chimpanzees , living their complex social lives in the wild , have helped more than anything else to make us realize we are part of , and not separated from , the amazing animals with whom we share the planet .	而這些黑猩猩 , 在野外生活著複雜的社會生活 , 幫助我們了解到我們是其中的一部分 , 和我們共享地球的神奇動物 。
so it's pretty sad to find that chimpanzees , like so many other creatures around the world , are losing their habitats .	所以 , 很可惜的是 , 發現黑猩猩 , 就像世界上許多其他生物一樣 , 正在失去牠們的棲息地 。
this is just one photograph from the air , and it shows you the forested highlands of gombe .	這只是空氣中的一張照片 , 它向你展示了森林高地的高地 。
and it was when i flew over the whole area , about 16 years ago , and realized that outside the park , this forest , which in 1960 had stretched almost unbroken along the eastern shore of lake tanganyika , which is where the tiny , 30squaremile gombe national park lies , that a question came to my mind .	當時我在16年前飛越整個區域 , 發現在公園外面的森林 , 在1960年 , 這片森林幾乎在坦尼卡的東岸 , 那裡有三十平方的美式足球場 , 全國公園就在我心中 。
" how can we even try to save these famous chimpanzees , when the people living around the national park are struggling to survive ? "	「 我們如何能拯救這些著名的黑猩猩 , 當住在國家公園附近的人們在掙扎生存的時候 ? 」
more people are living there than the land could possibly support .	比起土地能支援更多人 。
the numbers increased by refugees pouring in from burundi and over the lake from congo .	難民的數量增加 , 來自緬甸和剛果湖的數目 。
and very poor people they couldn't afford to buy food from elsewhere .	非常貧窮的人買不起其他地方的食物 。
this led to a program , which we call tacare .	這導致了一個計畫 , 我們稱之為tacare 。
it's a very holistic way of improving the lives of the people living in the villages around the park .	這是非常全面的改善居住在公園附近的村民的生活方式 。
it started small with 12 villages . it's now in 24 .	它從12個村莊開始 , 現在已經到了24年 。
there isn't time to go into it , but it's including things like tree nurseries , methods of farming most suitable to this now very degraded , almost desertlike land up in these mountains .	沒有時間深入探討 , 但它包括樹木護理器、農業方法 , 最適用於此 , 幾乎像沙漠般降落在這些山上 。
ways of controlling , preventing soil erosion .	控制的方式 , 防止土壤侵蝕 。
ways of reclaiming overused farmland , so that within two years they can again be productive .	重建過度使用的農地的方法 , 這樣在兩年內 , 它們就能再次發揮生產力 。
working to help the villagers obtain fresh water from wells .	努力協助村民從井裡取得淡水 。
perhaps build some schoolrooms .	也許建造了一些學校教室 。
most important of all , i believe , is working with small groups of women , providing them with opportunities for microcredit loans .	最重要的是 , 我相信 , 與一小群婦女合作 , 提供她們給微額貸款的機會 。
and we've got , as is the case around the world , about 95 percent of all loans returned .	我們的確有 , 世界各地有95%的貸款回報 。
empowering women , working with education , providing scholarships for girls so they can finish secondary school , in the clear understanding that , all around the world , as women's education improves , family size drops .	賦予婦女權力 , 和教育 , 提供獎學金給女孩 , 讓他們可以完成二年級的學校 , 明白的是 , 世界各地 , 隨著女性的教育改善 , 家庭規模降低 。
we provide information about family planning and about hiv/aids .	我們提供關於家庭規劃和愛滋病的資訊 。
and as a result of this program , something's happening for conservation .	由於這個計劃的結果 , 保育計畫正在發生 。
what's happening for conservation is that the farmers living in these 24 villages , instead of looking on us as a bunch of white people coming to study a whole bunch of monkeys and by the way , many of the staff are now tanzanian but when we began the tacare program , it was a tanzanian team going into the villages .	保育的原因是 , 那些住在24個村落的農民 , 不是把我們當成一群白人來研究一群猴子 , 順道一提 , 許多工人現在已經是坦尚尼人 , 但當我們開始停車計畫時 , 是個坦尚尼亞人進入村落 。
it was a tanzanian team talking to the villagers , asking what they were interested in .	這是一個坦尚尼亞的團隊 , 跟村民說話 , 問他們感興趣的是什麼 。
were they interested in conservation ? absolutely not .	他們對保育有興趣嗎 ? 絕對不是 。
they were interested in health ; they were interested in education .	他們對健康有興趣 , 他們對教育有興趣 。
and as time went on , and as their situation began to improve , they began to understand ever more about the need for conservation .	隨著時間過去 , 他們的情況開始改善 , 他們開始更了解保育的需求 。
they began to understand that as the upper levels of the hills were denuded of trees , so you've got this terrible soil erosion and mudslides .	他們開始了解 , 隨著山丘的上層水平被破壞了 , 所以你有種可怕的土壤侵蝕和泥塊 。
today , we are developing what we call the greater gombe ecosystem .	現今 , 我們正在發展所謂的更大的gombe生態系統 。
this is an area way outside the national park , stretching out into all these very degraded lands .	這是在國家公園以外的地方 , 延伸到這些非常退化的土地上 。
and as these villages have a better standard of life , they are actually agreeing to put between 10 percent and 20 percent of their land in the highlands aside , so that once again , as the trees grow back , the chimpanzees will have leafy corridors through which they can travel to interact as they must for genetic viability with other remnant groups outside the national park .	隨著這些村落有更好的生命標準 , 他們其實同意將百分之十到二十的土地放到高地 , 所以再一次的 , 隨著樹木長回來 , 黑猩猩會穿越葉綠色走廊 , 牠們可以和其他國家公園以外的遺傳能力交流 , 和其他國家公園以外的遺傳性 。
so tacare is a success .	所以 , 台灣是成功的 。
we're replicating it in other parts of africa , around other wilderness areas which are faced with extreme population pressure .	我們在非洲的其他地方複製它 , 其它的荒野 , 面臨極端人口壓力的地區 。
the problems in africa , however , as we've been discussing for the whole of these first couple of days of ted , are major problems .	然而 , 非洲的問題 , 正如我們一直在討論ted的前幾天 , 都是主要的問題 。
there is a great deal of poverty .	有很大的貧窮 。
and when you get large numbers of people living in land that is not that fertile , particularly when you cut down trees , and you leave the soil open to the wind for erosion , as desperate populations cut down more and more trees , so that they can try and grow food for themselves and their families , what's going to happen ? something's got to give .	當你有大量人居住在土地上 , 不是那麼肥沃 , 尤其是當你砍樹時 , 土壤會被風吹開 , 如絕望的族群砍下越來越多的樹 , 這樣他們就可以為自己和家人種食物 , 會發生什麼事 ? 一定要給他們 。
and the other problems in not only africa , but the rest of the developing world and , indeed , everywhere what are we doing to our planet ?	另外一個問題 , 不僅是非洲 , 還有其他發展中國家 , 還有 , 無所不在 , 我們對地球做了什麼事 ?
you know , the famous scientist , e . o . wilson said that if every person on this planet attains the standard of living of the average european or american , we need three new planets .	你知道 , 著名的科學家e.o.威爾森說 , 如果地球上每個人都能維持平均歐洲或美國人的平均壽命 , 我們需要三個新的行星 。
today , they are saying four . but we don't have them . we've got one .	今天 , 他們說的是四個 。 但我們沒有 。 我們有一個 。
and what's happened ? i mean , the question here is , here we are , arguably the most intelligent being that's ever walked planet earth , with this extraordinary brain , capable of the kind of technology that is so well illustrated by these ted conferences , and yet we're destroying the only home we have .	發生了什麼事 ? 我的意思是 , 問題來了 , 我們是地球上最聰明的生物 , 帶著這種非凡的大腦 , 能夠被ted大會所描述的科技所描述 , 但我們卻在摧毀我們唯一的家園 。
the indigenous people around the world , before they made a major decision , used to sit around and ask themselves , " how does this decision affect our people seven generations ahead ? "	世界各地的原住民 , 在他們做了一個重大決定之前 , 常常會自問: 「 這個決定會如何影響我們七個世代的人 ? 」
today , major decisions and i'm not particularly talking about africa here , but the developed world major decisions involving millions of dollars , and millions of people , are often based on , " how will this affect the next shareholders' meeting ? "	現今 , 主要決策和我不是特別在談論非洲 , 而是已開發國家的大決定 , 數百萬人 , 通常是基於: 「 這會如何影響下一個股東會議 ? 」
and these decisions affect africa .	這些決定會影響非洲 。
as i began traveling around africa talking about the problems faced by chimpanzees and their vanishing forests , i realized more and more how so many of africa's problems could be laid at the door of previous colonial exploitation .	當我開始在非洲四處旅行 , 談到黑猩猩和牠們消失的森林所面臨的問題時 , 我了解到更多的非洲問題可能是前殖民地剝削的門 。
so i began traveling outside africa , talking in europe , talking in the united states , going to asia .	所以我開始在非洲外遊 , 在歐洲和美國的談話 , 前往亞洲 。
and everywhere there were these terrible problems .	到處都有這些可怕的問題 。
and you know the kind i'm talking about . i'm talking about pollution .	你們知道我在說什麼 。 我說的是污染 。
the air that we breathe that often poisons us .	我們呼吸的空氣通常會毒害我們 。
the earth is poisoning our foods .	地球正在毒害我們的食物 。
the water water is perhaps one of the most crucial issues that we're going to face in this century and everywhere water is being polluted by agricultural , industrial and household chemicals that still are being sprayed around the world , seemingly with the inability to profit from past experience .	水可能是我們在這個世紀中所面臨的最關鍵議題之一 , 水被農業、工業和家庭的化學物質污染 , 仍然在世界各地散播著 , 似乎無法從過去的經驗中獲利 。
the mangroves are being cut down ; the effects of things like the tsunami get worse .	紅樹林被割掉 , 海嘯的效應變得更糟 。
we've talked about the soil erosion .	我們已經談過土壤侵蝕 。
we have the reckless burning of fossil fuels along with other greenhouse gasses , so called , leading to climate change .	我們還有燃燒化石燃料 , 還有其他溫室氣體 , 所以 , 導致氣候變遷 。
finally , all around the world , people have begun to believe that there is something going on very wrong with our climate .	最後 , 世界各地 , 人們開始相信 , 我們的氣候發生了很大的錯誤 。
all around the world climates are mixed up .	世界各地的氣候都混在一起了 。
and it's the poor people who are affected worse .	是影響更糟的窮人 。
it's africa that already is affected .	非洲已經受到影響 。
in many parts of subsaharan africa , the droughts are so much worse .	在撒哈拉以南非洲的許多地區 , 乾旱更糟 。
and when the rain does come , it so often leads to flooding and added distress , and the cycle of poverty and hunger and disease .	當雨季來臨時 , 它通常會造成洪水、加入痛苦 , 以及貧窮、飢餓和疾病的循環 。
and the numbers of people living in an area that the land cannot support , who are too poor to buy food , who can't move away because the whole land is degraded .	而住在一個無法支持土地的人數 , 他們太貧窮 , 無法買食物 , 因為整片土地被破壞了 。
and so you get desertification creeping , creeping , creeping as the last of the trees are cut down .	所以你會得到沙漠化的裂縫 , 哭泣 , 哭泣 , 隨著最後一棵樹被砍掉 。
and this kind of thing is not just in africa . it's all over the world .	這種東西不只在非洲 , 世界各地都一樣 。
so it wasn't surprising to me that as i was traveling around the world i met so many young people who seemed to have lost hope .	所以 , 我並不意外 , 當我在世界各地旅行時 , 我遇見了許多失望的年輕人 。
we seem to have lost wisdom , the wisdom of the indigenous people .	我們似乎失去智慧 , 原住民的智慧 。
i asked a question . " why ? "	我問了一個問題: 「 為什麼 ? 」
well , do you think there could be some kind of disconnect between this extraordinarily clever brain , the kind of brain that the ted technologies exemplify , and the human heart ? talking about it in the nonscientific term , in terms of love and compassion . is there some disconnect ?	嗯 , 你認為在這種非凡的聰明的大腦之間是否有某種程度的差異 ? ted科技的發展 , 人類的心 ? 用非科學的方式來談論它 , 用愛和同情心來談論它 , 有沒有關聯性 ?
and these young people , when i talk to them , basically they were either depressed or apathetic , or bitter and angry . and they said more or less the same thing , " we feel this way because we feel you've compromised our future and there's nothing we can do about it . "	這些年輕人 , 當我跟他們說話時 , 基本上 , 他們是沮喪、厭惡感、憤怒 。 他們說的 , 或多或少是同樣的話: 「 我們覺得你已經傷害了我們的未來 , 沒有我們能為它做的事 。 」
we have compromised their future .	我們已經破壞了他們的未來 。
i've got three little grandchildren , and every time i look at them and i think how we've harmed this beautiful planet since i was their age , i feel this desperation .	我有三個小孫子 , 每次我看著他們 , 我想我們如何傷害這個美麗的星球 , 我感覺到這絕望 。
and that led to this program we call roots and shoots , which began right here in tanzania and has now spread to 97 countries around the world .	這導致了我們稱之為根與芽的計畫 , 開始於坦尚尼亞 , 目前已經擴展到全世界97個國家 。
it's symbolic . roots make a firm foundation .	它是象徵性的 。 根會製造一間公司基金會 。
shoots seem tiny ; to reach the sun they can break through a brick wall .	射擊看起來很小 ; 抵達太陽 , 它們可以穿過磚牆 。
see the brick wall as all these problems we've inflicted on the planet , environmental and social . it's a message of hope .	把磚牆視為我們對地球造成的所有問題 , 環保和社會 。 它是希望的訊息 。
hundreds and thousands of young people around the world can break through and can make this a better world for all living things .	世界各地數以千計的年輕人可以通過 , 讓這個世界變得更美好 。
the most important message of roots and shoots: every single one of us makes a difference , every single day .	根部和芽的最重要的訊息:我們每一個人每天都能做出改變 。
we have a choice . every one of us in this room , we have a choice as to what kind of difference we want to make .	我們有選擇 。 在座的每個人 , 我們都有選擇要做什麼改變 。
the very poor have no choice . it's up to us to change things so that the poor have choice as well .	最貧窮的人無選擇 , 我們要改變現狀 , 才能讓窮人有選擇 。
the roots and shoots groups all choose three projects .	根和芽團體都選了三個項目 。
it depends on how old they are , and which country , whether they're in a city or rural , as to what kinds of projects .	它取決於它們的年齡 , 以及哪個國家 , 不論它們在城市或鄉村 , 都要歸功於什麼樣的計畫 。
but basically , we have programs now from preschool right through university , with more and more adults starting their own roots and shoots groups .	但基本上 , 我們有從幼兒園到大學的程式 , 越來越多的成年人開始自己的根源和芽群體 。
and every group chooses , between them , three different kinds of project to make this a better world , recognizing that all these different problems are interconnected and impinge on each other .	每一個團體都選擇 , 與他們之間 , 有三種不同的項目 , 讓這個世界變得更美好 , 認知到 , 所有這些不同的問題都互相連結 , 加強彼此 。
so one of their projects will be to help their own human community .	其中一個計畫是要協助他們自己的人類社群 。
and then , if they're able , they may raise money to help communities in other parts of the world .	然後 , 如果他們能夠 , 他們可能會募集資金 , 來協助世界其他地區的社區 。
one of their projects will be to help animals not just wildlife , domestic animals as well .	其中一個計畫是幫助動物 , 不只是野生動物 , 還有家畜 。
and one of their projects will be to help the environment that we all share .	其中一個計畫是要協助我們共享的環境 。
and woven throughout all of this is a message of learning to live in peace and harmony within ourselves , in our families , in our communities , between nations , between cultures , between religions and between us and the natural world .	一直以來 , 維也都在我們內心的和平和和諧中 , 在我們的家庭、我們的社區、國家之間、文化之間、宗教之間、和自然界之間 。
we need the natural world . we cannot go on destroying it at the rate we are .	我們需要自然世界 , 我們不能以我們的速度來摧毀它 。
we not do have more than this one planet .	我們沒有比這顆行星還多 。
just picking one or two of the projects right here in africa that the roots and shoots groups are doing , one or two projects only in tanzania , in uganda , kenya , south africa , congobrazzaville , sierra leone , cameroon and other groups . and as i say , it's in 97 countries around the world .	只是挑一個或兩個項目 , 非洲的根和芽群體都在做 , 只有在坦尚尼亞、烏干達、肯亞、南非、剛果利亞、獅子山共和國和其它團體 。 如我所說的 , 它是世界上97個國家 。
of course , they're planting trees . they're growing organic vegetables .	當然 , 他們在種樹 , 種植有機蔬菜 。
they're working in the refugee camps , with chickens and selling the eggs for a little amount of money , or just using them to feed their families , and feeling a sense of pride and empowerment , because they're no longer helpless and depending on others with their vegetables and their chickens .	他們在難民營工作 , 帶著雞來賣蛋 , 只用一些錢來餵養他們的家人 , 感覺到驕傲和自主權 , 因為他們不再無助 , 依靠他們吃蔬菜和雞肉 。
it's being used in uganda to give some psychological help to exchild soldiers .	它被用在烏干達 , 給予一些心理上的幫助 , 來給予童兵們 。
doing projects like this is bringing them out of themselves .	做這樣的項目 , 就是把他們自己帶出來 。
once again , they're useful members of society .	再一次 , 他們是社會中有用的成員 。
we have this program in prisons as well .	我們也在監獄中有這個計畫 。
so , there's no time for more roots and shoots now .	所以 , 現在沒有更多根和芽的時間了 。
but oh , they're also working on hiv/aids .	但 , 喔 , 他們也在研究愛滋病 。
that's a very important component of roots and shoots , with older kids talking to younger ones .	這是根和芽的成分 , 年紀較小的孩子對話是非常重要的 。
and unwanted pregnancies and things like that , which young people listen to better from other youth , rather than adults .	像這樣的懷孕和其他事情 , 年輕人會從其他青少年身上聽得更好 , 而不是成年人 。
hope . that's the question i get asked as i'm going around the world: " jane , you've seen so many terrible things , you've seen your chimpanzees decrease in number from about one million , at the turn of the century , to no more than 150 , 000 now , and the same with so many other animals .	希望 。 這就是我在世界各地被問到的問題: 「 珍 , 你看過這麼多可怕的事情 , 你已經看過你的黑猩猩 , 從一百萬 , 到一世紀 , 到現在沒有超過十五萬隻 , 和許多其他動物一樣 。
forests disappearing , deserts where once there was forest .	森林消失了 , 曾經有森林的沙漠 。
do you really have hope ? " well , yes .	你真的有希望嗎 ? 」 嗯 , 是的 。
you can't come to a conference like ted and not have hope , can you ?	你不能來參加像ted這樣的會議 , 沒有希望 , 你能嗎 ?
and of course , there's hope . one is this amazing human brain .	當然 , 還有希望 。 一個是令人驚嘆的人類大腦 。
and i mean , think of the technologies .	我的意思是 , 想想科技 。
and i've just been so thrilled , finally , to come to people talking about compost latrines .	最後 , 我很興奮 , 最後 , 要來談談合成的廁所 。
it's one of my hobbyhorses .	這是我的嗜好者之一 。
we just flush all this water down the lavatory , it's terrible .	我們剛剛把這些水流到電梯下面 , 很糟糕 。
and then talking about renewable energy desperately important .	接著 , 談到再生能源絕對重要 。
do we care about the planet for our children ?	我們是否在乎我們的孩子的星球 ?
how many of us have children or grandchildren , nieces , nephews ?	有多少人有孩子或孫子、姪子、姪子 ?
do we care about their future ?	我們在乎他們的未來嗎 ?
and if we care about their future , we , as the elite around the world , we can do something about it . we can make choices as to how we live each day .	如果我們在乎他們的未來 , 我們 , 身為世界各地的菁英 , 我們就能做點什麼 。 我們可以為我們每天的生活做些選擇 。
what we buy . what we wear .	我們買了什麼 , 穿什麼 。
and choose to make these choices with the question , how will this affect the environment around me ?	選擇用問題做出這些選擇 , 這會如何影響我身邊的環境 ?
how will it affect the life of my child when he or she grows up ?	當他或她長大後 , 會如何影響我的孩子的生活 ?
or my grandchild , or whatever it is .	或是我的孫子 , 不管它是什麼 。
so the human brain , coupled with the human heart , and we join hands around the world .	人類的大腦 , 與人類的心結合 , 我們加入了世界各地的手 。
and that's what ted is helping so well with , and google who help us , and esri are helping us with mapping in gombe national park .	這就是ted的幫助 , 和谷歌幫助我們 , esri正在幫我們繪製全國公園的地圖 。
all of these technologies we can use .	所有這些我們能使用的科技 。
now let's link them , and it's beginning to happen , isn't it ?	現在讓我們把它們連結起來 , 開始發生了 , 對吧 ?
you've heard about it this afternoon . it's beginning to happen .	你今天下午聽過這件事 , 開始發生了 。
this change , this change . to see change that we must have if we care about the future .	這種改變 , 這種改變 。 如果我們在乎未來 , 我們一定有改變 。
and the next reason for hope nature is amazingly resilient .	希望大自然的下一個理由是驚人的恢復力 。
you can take an area that's absolutely destroyed , with time and perhaps some help it can regenerate .	你可以拿一個完全摧毀的區域 , 帶著時間 , 或許有些幫助它可以再生 。
and an example is the tacare program .	舉個例子 , 就是 「 醫療計畫 」 。
i told you , where a seemingly dead tree stump if you stop hacking them for firewood , which you don't need to because you have wood lots , then in five years you can have a 30foot tree .	我跟你說 , 一個看似死的樹木 , 如果你停止砍伐樹木 , 你不需要因為你有很多木材 , 五年後 , 你就可以有30英尺高的樹 。
and animals , almost on the brink of extinction , can be given a second chance . that's my next book .	幾乎在滅絕的邊緣 , 可以得到第二次機會 。 這是我的下一本書 。
it's inspiring . and it brings me to my last category of hope , and we've heard about this so much in the last two days: this indomitable human spirit . this determination of people , the resilience of the human spirit , so that people who you would think would be battered by poverty , or disease , or whatever , can pull themselves up out of it , sometimes with a helping hand , and take their part in society , and take their part in changing the world .	它很鼓舞人心 。 它帶我到最後一類的希望 , 我們在過去的兩天中都聽過這麼多:這種不屈不撓的人類精神 。 這種人的韌性 , 使你認為會受到貧窮或疾病的影響 , 或疾病 , 或其他疾病的人們 , 可以自己脫離它 , 有時 , 帶著自己的力量 , 帶著他們的力量 , 帶領他們進入社會 , 參與改變世界 。
and just to think of one or two people out of africa who are just really inspiring .	想想非洲只有一兩個人真的很鼓舞人心 。
we could make a very long list , but obviously nelson mandela , emerging from 17 years of hard physical labor , 23 years of imprisonment , with this amazing ability to forgive , so that he could lead his nation out the evil regime of apartheid without a bloodbath .	我們可以做一個很長的清單 , 但很明顯地 , 曼德拉從17年的辛苦勞工興起 , 23年的監禁 , 帶著驚人的原諒能力 , 讓他能夠將種族隔離的邪惡政權帶出種族隔離 , 而不用血浴 。
ken sarowiwa , in nigeria , who took on the giant oil companies , and although people around the world tried their best , was executed .	奈及利亞的肯薩洛瓦採用巨型石油公司 , 儘管全世界的人都竭盡所能 , 卻被處決 。
people like this are so inspirational .	像這樣的人是如此鼓舞人心的 。
people like this are the role models we need for young africans .	像這樣的人是我們為非洲年輕人所需要的榜樣 。
and we need some environmental role models as well , and i've been hearing some of them today .	我們也需要一些環境的榜樣 , 我今天也在聽過其中一些例子 。
so i'm really grateful for this opportunity to share this message again , with everyone at ted .	所以我很感激這個機會再次分享這個訊息 , 和ted的每一個人 。
and i hope that some of us can get together and talk about some of these things , especially the roots and shoots program .	我希望我們當中有些人能聚在一起談論一些事情 , 尤其是根與芽計畫 。
and just a last word on that the young woman who's running this entire conference center , i met her today .	最後一個字 , 就是那個經營這整個會議中心的年輕女子 , 我今天遇見她 。
she came up so excited , with her certificate . she was [in] roots and shoots .	她很興奮 , 和她的證書成立 。 她是根和芽 。
she was in the leadership in dar es salaam .	她在達爾essalaam的領導階層 。
she said it's helped her to do what she's doing .	她說這幫助了她去做她在做的事 。
and it was very , very exciting for me to meet her and see just one example of how young people , when they are empowered , given the opportunity to take action , to make the world a better place , truly are our hope for tomorrow .	讓我很興奮地見到她 , 看到一個例子 , 說明年輕人是如何被賦予權力的 , 給予他們行動的機會 , 讓世界變得更美好 , 真正是我們未來的希望 。
artist dianna cohen shares some tough truths about plastic pollution in the ocean and in our lives and some thoughts on how to free ourselves from the plastic gyre .	藝術家dannacohen分享了一些關於海洋和海洋污染的艱難真理 , 以及我們生活中的一些想法 , 如何把我們從塑膠中解放出來 。
consumerism , global issues , green , mission blue , oceans , plastic	消費主義、全球議題、綠色、使命藍色、海洋、塑膠塑膠、塑膠 。
dianna cohen: tough truths about plastic pollution	黛安娜柯恩:對塑膠污染污染的棘手真相 。
i'm a visual artist , and i'm also one of the cofounders of the plastic pollution coalition .	我是視覺藝術家 , 我也是塑膠污染聯盟的共同創辦人之一 。
i've been working with plastic bags , which i cut up and sew back together as my primary material for my artwork for the last 20 years .	我和塑膠袋一起工作 , 在過去20年 , 我把它們切碎 , 再縫合成我的藝術品 。
