we know from the framingham studies , that if your three best friends are obese there is a 50 percent better chance that you'll be overweight .	我們從弗萊明罕的研究得知 , 如果你的三個最好的朋友過胖了50%的機會你會過重 。
so , if you hang out with unhealthy people , that's going to have a measurable impact over time .	所以 , 如果你和不健康的人在一起 , 會隨著時間產生可測量的影響 。
instead , if your friend's idea of recreation is physical activity , bowling , or playing hockey , biking or gardening , if your friends drink a little , but not too much , and they eat right , and they're engaged , and they're trusting and trustworthy , that is going to have the biggest impact over time .	取而代之的是 , 如果你的朋友對娛樂的看法是實體的活動 , 包林 , 或演奏曲棍球 , 如果你的朋友喝一點點 , 但卻不太喜歡 , 他們會吃得對 , 而且他們很有信任和信任感 , 那會隨著時間產生最大的影響 。
diets don't work . no diet in the history of the world has ever worked for more than two percent of the population .	飲食是行不通的 , 世界歷史上沒有飲食 , 超過2%的人口 。
exercise programs usually start in january ; they're usually done by october .	運動計畫通常在一月開始 , 通常是十月時完成的 。
when it comes to longevity there is no short term fix in a pill or anything else .	當談到長壽時 , 沒有短期的條件在藥丸或其他其他的條件 。
but when you think about it , your friends are longterm adventures , and therefore , perhaps the most significant thing you can do to add more years to your life , and life to your years . thank you very much .	但當你仔細想想 , 你的朋友是長期的冒險 , 因此 , 或許是你能做的最重要的事 , 把更多年加入人生 , 多年 , 非常謝謝你 。
ink that conducts electricity ; a window that turns from clear to opaque at the flip of a switch ; a jelly that makes music . all this stuff exists , and catarina mota says: it's time to play with it . mota leads us on a tour of surprising and cool new materials , and suggests that the way we'll figure out what they're good for is to experiment , tinker and have fun .	引發電力的墨水 ; 一扇窗戶 , 從明顯轉移到開關的光滑 ; 一顆製造音樂的水母 。 所有這些東西都存在 , 而卡塔說是時候玩的 。 莫塔帶領我們到驚喜和酷的新材料 , 並且建議我們想出它們的好處 , 做實驗、補丁和有樂趣 。
creativity , design , technology	創意、設計、科技、科技、科技 。
catarina mota: play with smart materials	catarinamota:用聰明的材料玩耍 。
i have a friend in portugal whose grandfather built a vehicle out of a bicycle and a washing machine so he could transport his family .	我在葡萄牙有個朋友 , 他的祖父用腳踏車建造了一台車 , 一台洗衣機 , 可以運送他的家人 。
he did it because he couldn't afford a car , but also because he knew how to build one .	他這麼做是因為他負擔不起車 , 也因為他知道如何建造一台車 。
there was a time when we understood how things worked and how they were made , so we could build and repair them , or at the very least make informed decisions about what to buy .	曾有一段時間 , 我們明白事情是如何運作的 , 及它們是如何製造和修復 , 或最少有知情的決策 , 來決定要買什麼 。
many of these doityourself practices were lost in the second half of the 20th century .	許多這些多樣性練習在20世紀後半葉就失去了 。
but now , the maker community and the opensource model are bringing this kind of knowledge about how things work and what they're made of back into our lives , and i believe we need to take them to the next level , to the components things are made of .	但現在 , 製造者群和開放原始碼模型正帶著這種知識 , 了解事物如何運作 , 以及它們如何組成我們的生命 , 我相信我們需要把它們帶到下一個層 , 到下一個階段 , 來組成物件 。
for the most part , we still know what traditional materials like paper and textiles are made of and how they are produced .	大部分時候 , 我們仍然知道傳統的材料 , 例如紙和紡織品是如何製成的 , 以及它們如何產生 。
but now we have these amazing , futuristic composites plastics that change shape , paints that conduct electricity , pigments that change color , fabrics that light up .	但現在我們有了這些驚人的 , 具體的組成塑膠 , 可以改變形狀 , 顏色會改變顏色的顏料 , 可以亮起來的結構 。
let me show you some examples .	讓我給你們看一些例子 。
so conductive ink allows us to paint circuits instead of using the traditional printed circuit boards or wires .	導電墨能讓我們繪製電路 , 而不是使用傳統印刷電路板或電線 。
in the case of this little example i'm holding , we used it to create a touch sensor that reacts to my skin by turning on this little light .	在我握住的這個小例子中 , 我們用它來製造觸感感感感應器 , 來對我的皮膚做出反應 。
conductive ink has been used by artists , but recent developments indicate that we will soon be able to use it in laser printers and pens .	藝術家的誘導墨水已經被使用 , 但最近的發展顯示 , 我們很快就能用在雷射印表機和筆上 。
and this is a sheet of acrylic infused with colorless lightdiffusing particles .	這張是一張白紙 , 上面裝滿了無色的發光粒子 。
what this means is that , while regular acrylic only diffuses light around the edges , this one illuminates across the entire surface when i turn on the lights around it .	這意味著 , 雖然一般的加密方式只會在邊緣散射光 , 但當我打開它周圍的光線時 , 這個光會照亮整個表面 。
two of the known applications for this material include interior design and multitouch systems .	這個材料中有兩個已知的應用 , 包括內部設計和多觸控系統 。
and thermochromic pigments change color at a given temperature .	溫度的色素改變了特定溫度的顏色 。
so i'm going to place this on a hot plate that is set to a temperature only slightly higher than ambient and you can see what happens .	所以我要把這個裝置放在一個較高溫的板子上 , 溫度只有稍高一點 , 你可以看到發生了什麼事 。
so one of the principle applications for this material is , amongst other things , in baby bottles , so it indicates when the contents are cool enough to drink .	所以 , 這種材料的其中一個原則是 , 在其他東西之中 , 在嬰兒瓶子裡 , 它表示內容很酷 , 可以喝得喝 。
so these are just a few of what are commonly known as smart materials .	這些只是我們所知的智慧材料 。
in a few years , they will be in many of the objects and technologies we use on a daily basis .	幾年後 , 它們會出現在我們每天使用的物品和技術中 。
we may not yet have the flying cars science fiction promised us , but we can have walls that change color depending on temperature , keyboards that roll up , and windows that become opaque at the flick of a switch .	我們可能還沒能有科幻小說的飛行車 , 但我們還能有改變顏色的牆 , 根據溫度 , 鍵盤上滾動 , 窗戶會變得不平常 。
so i'm a social scientist by training , so why am i here today talking about smart materials ?	我是社會科學家 , 為什麼我今天要談智慧材料 ?
well first of all , because i am a maker .	首先 , 因為我是個製造家 。
i'm curious about how things work and how they are made , but also because i believe we should have a deeper understanding of the components that make up our world , and right now , we don't know enough about these hightech composites our future will be made of .	我很好奇事物是如何運作的 , 也是因為我相信我們應該更深入了解我們的世界的元件 , 而現在 , 我們對這些高科技複合物的未來是不夠的 。
smart materials are hard to obtain in small quantities .	智慧材料很難在小量中取得 。
there's barely any information available on how to use them , and very little is said about how they are produced .	幾乎沒有任何資訊可以用來使用它們 , 幾乎沒有提到它們是如何產生的 。
so for now , they exist mostly in this realm of trade secrets and patents only universities and corporations have access to .	目前為止 , 他們主要存在於貿易秘密和專利制度的領域 , 只有大學和企業才能取得 。
so a little over three years ago , kirsty boyle and i started a project we called open materials .	三年前 , 科斯泰男孩和我創立了一個計畫 , 我們稱之為 「 開放材料 」 。
it's a website where we , and anyone else who wants to join us , share experiments , publish information , encourage others to contribute whenever they can , and aggregate resources such as research papers and tutorials by other makers like ourselves .	它是一個網站 , 我們和任何想要加入我們的人 , 分享實驗 , 發表資訊 , 鼓勵其他人 , 無論何時能貢獻 , 例如研究論文和教學者 , 像我們一樣的製造者 。
we would like it to become a large , collectively generated database of doityourself information on smart materials .	我們希望它能成為一個龐大、集體的資料庫 , 可以用智慧型材料來產生資訊 。
but why should we care how smart materials work and what they are made of ?	但為什麼我們要關心聰明的材料是如何運作的 ? 及它們是由什麼組成的 ?
first of all , because we can't shape what we don't understand , and what we don't understand and use ends up shaping us .	首先 , 因為我們無法形塑我們不了解的 , 最後我們不了解和使用的卻塑造了我們 。
the objects we use , the clothes we wear , the houses we live in , all have a profound impact on our behavior , health and quality of life .	我們所使用的物品、穿的衣服、我們所住的房子 , 都對我們的行為、健康和生活品質有很深的影響 。
so if we are to live in a world made of smart materials , we should know and understand them .	所以 , 如果我們要活在一個由智慧材料組成的世界 , 我們應該要知道、了解它們 。
secondly , and just as important , innovation has always been fueled by tinkerers .	第二 , 同樣重要的是 , 創新一直都是由補丁者所組成的 。
so many times , amateurs , not experts , have been the inventors and improvers of things ranging from mountain bikes to semiconductors , personal computers , airplanes .	很多時候 , 業餘人士 , 不是專家 , 都是發明家和改善的東西 , 從山腳踏車到半導體、個人電腦、飛機 。
the biggest challenge is that material science is complex and requires expensive equipment .	最大的挑戰是 , 材料科學是複雜且需要昂貴的設備 。
but that's not always the case .	但事實並非如此 。
two scientists at university of illinois understood this when they published a paper on a simpler method for making conductive ink .	伊利諾大學的兩個科學家明白這一點 , 當他們發表一篇文章 , 用比較簡單的方式來製作導電墨水 。
jordan bunker , who had had no experience with chemistry until then , read this paper and reproduced the experiment at his maker space using only offtheshelf substances and tools .	jordanbunker , 直到那時 , 他完全沒有化學經驗 , 讀了這篇論文 , 並在他的製造者空間中重複這個實驗 , 只用現成的物質和工具 。
he used a toaster oven , and he even made his own vortex mixer , based on a tutorial by another scientist/maker .	他用烤箱 , 甚至製作了自己的呼吸道混合器 , 根據另一個科學家/製造者的教學 。
jordan then published his results online , including all the things he had tried and didn't work , so others could study and reproduce it .	約旦接著發表他的結果在網路上 , 包括他曾經嘗試過的所有事情 , 沒有用 , 其他人可以研究和複製它 。
so jordan's main form of innovation was to take an experiment created in a wellequipped lab at the university and recreate it in a garage in chicago using only cheap materials and tools he made himself .	所以 , 約旦的主要創新形式是把一個在大學有資格的實驗室拿來做實驗 , 在芝加哥的一個車庫裡 , 只用便宜的材料和工具 , 讓他自己做出 。
and now that he published this work , others can pick up where he left and devise even simpler processes and improvements .	現在他發表了這個作品 , 其他人可以從他左下方 , 想像更簡單的過程和改善 。
another example i'd like to mention her project's goal is to highlight the expressive qualities of materials while focusing on the creativity and skills of the builder .	另外一個例子 , 我想要提到她的專案目標是強調材料的表達品質 , 同時專注在建造者的創造力和技能 。
electronics kits are very powerful in that they teach us how things work , but the constraints inherent in their design influence the way we learn .	電子裝置對我們來說是非常強大的 , 它們教導我們事情是如何運作的 , 但它們的設計的限制會影響我們學習的方式 。
so hannah's approach , on the other hand , is to formulate a series of techniques for creating unusual objects that free us from predesigned constraints by teaching us about the materials themselves .	另一方面 , 漢娜的手法是要設計一系列的技術 , 來創造出不尋常的物品 , 讓我們免於預先設定的限制 , 教導我們材料本身 。
so amongst hannah's many impressive experiments , this is one of my favorites .	漢娜有很多令人印象深刻的實驗 , 這是我最喜歡的一個 。
[ " paper speakers " ] what we're seeing here is just a piece of paper with some copper tape on it connected to an mp3 player and a magnet .	我們現在看到的只是一張紙 , 上面有一些銅膠帶 , 連接到mp3玩家和磁鐵 。
so based on the research by marcelo coelho from mit , hannah created a series of paper speakers out of a wide range of materials from simple copper tape to conductive fabric and ink .	所以 , 根據麻省理工學院的馬塞羅柯爾研究 , 漢娜創造了一系列的紙喇叭 , 來自廣泛的銅膠、導電布和墨水 。
just like jordan and so many other makers , hannah published her recipes and allows anyone to copy and reproduce them .	就像約旦和許多其他製造者一樣 , 漢娜發表了她的食譜 , 允許任何人複製和繁殖 。
but paper electronics is one of the most promising branches of material science in that it allows us to create cheaper and flexible electronics .	但紙電子學是最有前景的材料科學分支之一 , 讓我們能創造出更便宜、更靈活的電子產品 。
so hannah's artisanal work , and the fact that she shared her findings , opens the doors to a series of new possibilities that are both aesthetically appealing and innovative .	所以漢娜的手工藝作品 , 她分享了她的發現 , 把一連串的門打開了一系列的新可能 , 兩者都是美感和創新 。
so the interesting thing about makers is that we create out of passion and curiosity , and we are not afraid to fail .	製造者有趣的是 , 我們創造出熱情和好奇心 , 我們不怕失敗 。
we often tackle problems from unconventional angles , and , in the process , end up discovering alternatives or even better ways to do things .	我們經常處理非傳統的角度問題 , 在過程中 , 最終發現了替代方案 , 甚至更好的方式來做事 。
so the more people experiment with materials , the more researchers are willing to share their research , and manufacturers their knowledge , the better chances we have to create technologies that truly serve us all .	所以越多人實驗材料 , 研究人員願意分享他們的研究 , 製造商他們的知識 , 我們就越有可能創造出真正服務我們所有人的科技 。
so i feel a bit as ted nelson must have when , in the early 1970s , he wrote , " you must understand computers now . "	所以 , 我覺得tednelson在1970年代早期 , 他寫道: 「 你現在一定要了解電腦 。 」
back then , computers were these large mainframes only scientists cared about , and no one dreamed of even having one at home .	當時 , 電腦只是這些大型的主體 , 只有科學家在乎 , 甚至沒有人在家中有一次 。
so it's a little strange that i'm standing here and saying , " you must understand smart materials now . "	所以 , 我站在這裡有點奇怪 , 說: 「 你現在必須要了解智慧材料 。 」
just keep in mind that acquiring preemptive knowledge about emerging technologies is the best way to ensure that we have a say in the making of our future .	請記住 , 取得新興科技的先前知識是確保我們能在未來發聲的最佳方式 。
when we drive , we get into a glass bubble , lock the doors and press the accelerator , relying on our eyes to guide us even though we can only see the few cars ahead of and behind us . but what if cars could share data with each other about their position and velocity , and use predictive models to calculate the safest routes for everyone on the road ? jennifer healey imagines a world without accidents .	當我們開車時 , 我們進入一個玻璃泡 , 鎖上門和加速器 , 靠我們的眼睛引導我們 , 儘管我們只能看到在我們身後的幾輛車 。 但如果車子能和彼此分享他們的位置和速度 , 用預測模型來計算路上所有人的安全路線 ? 珍妮佛.華利想像一個沒有意外的世界 。
jennifer healey: if cars could talk , accidents might be avoidable	珍妮佛:如果車子能說話 , 意外可能是避免的 。
let's face it: driving is dangerous .	讓我們面對現實吧:開車是危險的 。
it's one of the things that we don't like to think about , but the fact that religious icons and good luck charms show up on dashboards around the world betrays the fact that we know this to be true .	這是我們不喜歡思考的一件事 , 但 , 宗教的象徵和好運迷思出現在世界各地的儀表上 , 背叛我們知道這是真的 。
car accidents are the leading cause of death in people ages 16 to 19 in the united states leading cause of death and 75 percent of these accidents have nothing to do with drugs or alcohol .	車禍是16到19歲的死亡人數最高的成因 , 在美國 , 造成死亡 , 75%的意外與毒品或酒精無關 。
no one can say for sure , but i remember my first accident .	沒有人可以說是肯定的 , 但我記得我的第一個意外 。
i was a young driver out on the highway , and the car in front of me , i saw the brake lights go on .	我在高速公路上擔任年輕的司機 , 前面的車子 , 我看到了煞車燈亮了 。
i'm like , " okay , all right , this guy is slowing down , i'll slow down too . "	我說: 「 好吧 , 這個傢伙慢下來 , 我也會慢下來 。 」
i step on the brake .	我踏上煞車 。
but no , this guy isn't slowing down .	但 , 不 , 這個傢伙並沒有慢下來 。
this guy is stopping , dead stop , dead stop on the highway .	這個傢伙在高速公路停下來 , 死了 , 停下來 。
it was just going 65 to zero ?	只剩下65到0 ?
i slammed on the brakes .	我在煞車上滑雪 。
i felt the abs kick in , and the car is still going , and it's not going to stop , and i know it's not going to stop , and the air bag deploys , the car is totaled , and fortunately , no one was hurt .	我覺得這個荒唐的車還在前進 , 它不會停下來 , 我知道它不會停車 , 空氣袋部署 , 很幸運的是 , 沒有人會受傷 。
but i had no idea that car was stopping , and i think we can do a lot better than that .	但我完全不知道車停下來了 , 我想我們能做得更好 。
i think we can transform the driving experience by letting our cars talk to each other .	我認為我們可以改變駕駛經驗 , 讓車子彼此對話 。
i just want you to think a little bit about what the experience of driving is like now .	我希望各位稍微思考一下開車的體驗 。
get into your car . close the door . you're in a glass bubble .	走進你的車子 , 關上門 , 你在玻璃泡泡中 。
you can't really directly sense the world around you .	你無法直覺周遭的世界 。
you're in this extended body .	你身在這個延伸的身體裡 。
you're tasked with navigating it down partiallyseen roadways , in and amongst other metal giants , at superhuman speeds .	你的任務是將它導航到一部分的路道上 , 進而在其他金屬巨人當中 , 以超人速度 。
okay ? and all you have to guide you are your two eyes .	好嗎 ? 你只需要引導你兩個眼睛 。
okay , so that's all you have , eyes that weren't really designed for this task , but then people ask you to do things like , you want to make a lane change , what's the first thing they ask you do ?	好吧 , 這就是你所擁有的眼睛 , 不是真的為了這個任務而設計的 , 但人們會問你做些什麼 , 你想做出改變 , 第一個他們要你做的是什麼 ?
take your eyes off the road . that's right .	把你的眼睛從路上拿走 , 沒錯 。
stop looking where you're going , turn , check your blind spot , and drive down the road without looking where you're going .	別再看你要去哪裡 , 轉過來 , 檢查你的盲點 , 不看你要去哪裡 。
you and everyone else . this is the safe way to drive .	你和其他人 。 這是安全的駕駛方式 。
why do we do this ? because we have to , we have to make a choice , do i look here or do i look here ?	我們為什麼要這樣做呢 ? 因為我們必須做選擇 , 我看這裡 , 還是看這裡 ?
and usually we do a fantastic job picking and choosing what we attend to on the road .	通常 , 我們會在路上做一個很棒的挑選和選擇我們要在路上做的事 。
but occasionally we miss something .	但偶爾我們會錯過某樣東西 。
occasionally we sense something wrong or too late .	偶爾 , 我們會感覺錯了或太晚 。
in countless accidents , the driver says , " i didn't see it coming . "	在無數的意外中 , 司機說: 「 我看不到它會來 。 」
and i believe that . i believe that .	我相信 , 我相信 。
we can only watch so much .	我們只能看這麼多 。
but the technology exists now that can help us improve that .	但現在科技的存在可以幫助我們改善這一點 。
in the future , with cars exchanging data with each other , we will be able to see not just three cars ahead and three cars behind , to the right and left , all at the same time , bird's eye view , we will actually be able to see into those cars .	在未來 , 車子彼此交換資料 , 我們不僅可以看見三輛車後面還有三輛車 , 再往右邊 , 再左邊看 , 鳥的眼睛 , 我們將能夠看到這些車子 。
we will be able to see the velocity of the car in front of us , to see how fast that guy's going or stopping .	我們將能夠看見前面車輛的速度 , 看看那人的速度有多快或停止 。
if that guy's going down to zero , i'll know .	如果那個人下降到零 , 我就會知道 。
and with computation and algorithms and predictive models , we will be able to see the future .	透過計算、演算法和預測模型 , 我們就能看見未來 。
you may think that's impossible .	你可能認為不可能 。
how can you predict the future ? that's really hard .	你要如何預測未來 ? 這真的很難 。
actually , no . with cars , it's not impossible .	事實上 , 沒有 。 車子沒有 , 不可能 。
cars are threedimensional objects that have a fixed position and velocity .	車子是三維的物體 , 有固定的位置和速度 。
they travel down roads .	他們沿著道路走 。
often they travel on prepublished routes .	通常 , 他們會在出版的路線上旅行 。
it's really not that hard to make reasonable predictions about where a car's going to be in the near future .	要在不久的將來 , 要做出合理的預測是不難的 。
even if , when you're in your car and some motorcyclist comes bshoom ! 85 miles an hour down , lanesplitting i know you've had this experience that guy didn't " just come out of nowhere . "	就算你在車上 , 有些機車騎士來了bsshoom ! 85英里 , 我知道你有過這種經驗 , 那個傢伙沒出門了 。
that guy's been on the road probably for the last half hour .	那個人在路上大概是半小時 。
right ? i mean , somebody's seen him .	對吧 ? 我的意思是 , 有人看過他 。
ten , 20 , 30 miles back , someone's seen that guy , and as soon as one car sees that guy and puts him on the map , he's on the map position , velocity , good estimate he'll continue going 85 miles an hour .	10、20、30英哩後 , 有人看過那個人 , 一旦看到那個人 , 把他放在地圖上 , 他在地圖上的位置、速度 , 好估計他會以時速持續85英哩 。
you'll know , because your car will know , because that other car will have whispered something in his ear , like , " by the way , five minutes , motorcyclist , watch out . "	你會知道 , 因為你的車會知道 , 因為其他車子會在他的耳朵裡對某樣東西說: 「 順便一提 , 五分鐘 , 摩托車騎士 , 看看 。 」
you can make reasonable predictions about how cars behave .	你可以針對汽車的行為做出合理的預測 。
i mean , they're newtonian objects .	我的意思是 , 它們是牛頓的物品 。
that's very nice about them .	這對他們來說是很棒的 。
so how do we get there ?	所以 , 我們要如何達成目標 ?
we can start with something as simple as sharing our position data between cars , just sharing gps .	我們可以從簡單的開始 , 如同分享汽車之間的位置資料 , 只要分享gps 。
if i have a gps and a camera in my car , i have a pretty precise idea of where i am and how fast i'm going .	如果我在車上有gps和攝影機 , 我對於我在哪裡 , 以及我要走得多快 。
with computer vision , i can estimate where the cars around me are , sort of , and where they're going .	有了電腦視覺 , 我可以估計我身邊的汽車在哪裡 , 有點像是在哪裡 。
and same with the other cars .	另一輛車也一樣 。
they can have a precise idea of where they are , and sort of a vague idea of where the other cars are .	它們可以精確地看出它們在哪裡 , 有點模糊地看其他車子的位置 。
what happens if two cars share that data , if they talk to each other ?	如果兩輛車共享資料 , 如果他們彼此交談 , 會發生什麼事 ?
i can tell you exactly what happens .	我可以告訴你們發生了什麼事 。
professor bob wang and his team have done computer simulations of what happens when fuzzy estimates combine , even in light traffic , when cars just share gps data , and we've moved this research out of the computer simulation and into robot test beds that have the actual sensors that are in cars now on these robots: stereo cameras , gps , and the twodimensional laser range finders that are common in backup systems .	鮑勃.威爾斯教授和他的團隊做了電腦模擬 , 當模糊的估計結合時 , 甚至在光線交通時 , 汽車只是分享gps資料 , 我們把這項研究從電腦模擬中移到機械測試 , 裡面有現在車子裡的感應器:stepho、gps , 和2d雷射雷射雷射探測器在後備系統中是常見的 。
we also attach a discrete shortrange communication radio , and the robots talk to each other .	我們也將一個異常的通訊無線電連接在一起 , 機器人彼此對話 。
when these robots come at each other , they track each other's position precisely , and they can avoid each other .	當這些機器人彼此接近時 , 它們會精確地追蹤彼此的位置 , 它們就能避免彼此 。
we're now adding more and more robots into the mix , and we encountered some problems .	我們現在在混合中加入越來越多的機器人 , 我們遇到了一些問題 。
one of the problems , when you get too much chatter , it's hard to process all the packets , so you have to prioritize , and that's where the predictive model helps you .	其中一個問題 , 當你收到太多的聊天 , 很難處理所有的包裝 , 所以你得先順序 , 這就是預測模式能幫助你 。
if your robot cars are all tracking the predicted trajectories , you don't pay as much attention to those packets .	如果你的機械車都在追蹤預測軌跡 , 你就不會注意到那些包裝 。
you prioritize the one guy who seems to be going a little off course .	你把一個看起來有點偏離課程的人列為優先順序 。
that guy could be a problem .	那傢伙可能是個問題 。
and you can predict the new trajectory .	你可以預測新的軌跡 。
so you don't only know that he's going off course , you know how .	所以你不只知道他要上課 , 你知道怎麼做 。
and you know which drivers you need to alert to get out of the way .	你也知道你需要警告哪個司機 , 才能走出這條路 。
and we wanted to do how can we best alert everyone ?	我們想做我們如何能警告每個人 ?
how can these cars whisper , " you need to get out of the way ? "	這些車如何能輕聲地說: 「 你需要走出路 ? 」
well , it depends on two things: one , the ability of the car , and second the ability of the driver .	嗯 , 它取決於兩件事:第一 , 汽車的能力 , 第二是駕駛的能力 。
if one guy has a really great car , but they're on their phone or , you know , doing something , they're not probably in the best position to react in an emergency .	如果一個人有一台很棒的車 , 但他們在手機上 , 或你知道的 , 他們可能不會在緊急情況下做出最好的反應 。
so we started a separate line of research doing driver state modeling .	所以我們開始了一系列的研究 , 做駕駛式的模型 。
and now , using a series of three cameras , we can detect if a driver is looking forward , looking away , looking down , on the phone , or having a cup of coffee .	現在 , 使用一系列的三台攝影機 , 我們可以偵測一個駕駛向前看 , 向下看 , 手機或喝杯咖啡 。
we can predict the accident and we can predict who , which cars , are in the best position to move out of the way to calculate the safest route for everyone .	我們可以預測意外 , 我們可以預測誰 , 哪個車子是最好的位置 , 可以從最好的方向走出來 , 來計算每個人最安全的路線 。
fundamentally , these technologies exist today .	基本上 , 這些技術今天存在 。
i think the biggest problem that we face is our own willingness to share our data .	我認為我們所面臨的最大問題是我們願意分享我們的資料 。
i think it's a very disconcerting notion , this idea that our cars will be watching us , talking about us to other cars , that we'll be going down the road in a sea of gossip .	我認為這是一個非常令人不安的概念 , 我們的車子會看著我們 , 談到其他車子 , 我們會在八卦的海中走下路 。
but i believe it can be done in a way that protects our privacy , just like right now , when i look at your car from the outside , i don't really know about you .	但我相信它可以用保護我們的隱私的方式來做 , 就像現在 , 當我看著你的車子從外面看 , 我並不知道你 。
if i look at your license plate number , i don't really know who you are .	如果我看一下你的車牌號碼 , 我並不知道你是誰 。
i believe our cars can talk about us behind our backs .	我相信我們的車可以在我們的背後談論我們 。
and i think it's going to be a great thing .	我認為這將會是一件很棒的事 。
i want you to consider for a moment if you really don't want the distracted teenager behind you to know that you're braking , that you're coming to a dead stop .	我希望你能考慮一下 , 如果你不想背後的青少年 , 知道你在煞車 , 你要停下來 。
by sharing our data willingly , we can do what's best for everyone .	藉著意願分享我們的資料 , 我們就能為每個人做最好的事 。
so let your car gossip about you .	所以 , 讓你的車子八卦吧 。
it's going to make the roads a lot safer .	它會讓道路變得更安全 。
x prize founder peter diamandis talks about how he helped stephen hawking fulfill his dream of going to space by flying together into the upper atmosphere and experiencing weightlessness at zero g .	xprizes創辦人彼得•戴曼迪斯談到他如何幫助史蒂芬•霍金去到太空的夢想 , 通過一起飛進上層的大氣 , 體驗無重力 。
business , flight , science , short talk , space , technology , universe	商業、飛行、科學、短談話、太空科技、宇宙、宇宙、宇宙 。
peter diamandis on stephen hawking in zero g	史蒂芬•戴曼迪斯在史蒂芬•霍金的0年 , 史蒂芬•霍金 。
those of you who know me know how passionate i am about opening the space frontier .	認識我的人知道我對於打開太空的領域有多熱情 。
so when i had the chance to give the world's expert in gravity the experience of zero gravity , it was incredible .	所以當我有機會給全世界的重力專家--0重力的體驗 , 真是不可思議 。
and i want to tell you that story .	我想告訴各位這個故事 。
i first met him through the archon x prize for genomics .	我第一次見到他 , 看了基因組學的獎項 。
it's a competition we're holding , the second x prize , for the first team to sequence 100 human genomes in 10 days .	這是我們所舉辦的一項競賽 , 第二個xprize , 在十天內 , 第一個人基因組測序的團隊 。
we have something called the genome 100 100 individuals we're sequencing as part of that .	我們有一個叫做基因組的一百個人 , 我們將其定位為其中的一部分 。
craig venter chairs that event .	克萊格•凡特會議的椅子 。
and i met professor hawking , and he said his dream was to travel into space .	我遇見了霍金教授 , 他說他的夢想是進入太空 。
and i said , " i can't take you there , but i can take you into weightlessness into zerog .	我說: 「 我不能帶你去那裡 , 但我可以把你帶到零度上 。
and he said , on the spot , " absolutely , yes . "	然後他說: 「 絕對是的 。 」
well , the only way to experience zerog on earth is actually with parabolic flight , weightless flight .	世界上唯一能體驗到零的唯一方法 , 實際上是用拋物的飛行 , 無重力飛行 。
you take an airplane , you fly over the top , you're weightless for 25 seconds .	你搭飛機 , 飛越上方 , 體重不到25秒 。
come back down , you weigh twice as much .	回來看看 , 你的體重是兩倍 。
you do it again and again .	你一次又一次的做 。
you can get eight , 10 minutes of weightlessness how nasa's trained their astronauts for so long .	你可以得到8、10分鐘的無重量 , 美國太空總署對太空人的訓練有多久 。
we set out to do this .	我們開始這樣做 。
it took us 11 years to become operational .	我們花了11年才開始營運 。
and we announced that we were going to fly stephen hawking .	我們宣佈我們要飛史蒂芬霍金 。
we had one government agency and one company aircraft operator say , you're crazy , don't do that , you're going kill the guy .	我們有一間政府機構 , 一家公司的飛機操作員說 , 你瘋了 , 別這樣做 , 你要殺了這個人 。
and he wanted to go .	他想去 。
we worked hard to get all the permissions .	我們努力取得所有許可 。
and six months later , we sat down at kennedy space center .	六個月後 , 我們坐在甘迺迪太空中心 。
we had a press conference , we announced our intent to do one zerog parabola , give him 25 seconds of zerog .	我們有一個新聞研討會 , 我們宣佈我們的意圖要做1個0降落傘 , 給他25秒的零 。
and if it went really well , we might do three parabolas .	如果真的成功了 , 我們可能會做三台降落傘 。
well , we asked him why he wanted to go up and do this .	我們問他 , 他為什麼要上去做這件事 。
and what he said , for me , was very moving .	他對我說的 , 是非常動人的 。
he said , " life on earth is at an everincreasing risk of being wiped out by disaster . . .	他說: 「 地球上的生命 , 造成災難性的增加 ,
i think the human race doesn't have a future if it doesn't go into space .	我認為如果人類不進入太空 , 人類就沒有未來 。
i therefore want to encourage public interest in space . "	所以我想鼓勵大眾對空間的興趣 。 」
we took him out to the kennedy space center , up inside the nasa vehicle , into the back of the zerog airplane .	我們把他帶到甘迺迪太空中心 , 到太空總署的車內 , 到零下飛機的後面 。
we had about 20 people who made donations we raised $150 , 000 in donations for children's charities who flew with us .	我們有大約20個人捐款 , 我們募集了15萬美金的捐款給那些與我們一起飛行的兒童慈善機構 。
a few tedsters here .	這裡有幾個tedster 。
we set up a whole er .	我們成立了一整個急診室 。
we had four emergency room doctors and two nurses on board the airplane .	我們有四個急診室醫生 , 兩位護士在飛機上 。
we were monitoring his po2 of his blood , his heart rate , his blood pressure .	我們在監視他的血液、他的心跳、他的血壓 。
we had everything all set in case of an emergency ; god knows , you don't want to hurt this worldrenowned expert .	我們所有的事都設定在緊急情況下 , 上帝知道 , 你不想傷害這個世界知名的專家 。
we took off from the shuttle landing facility , where the shuttle takes off and lands .	我們從太空梭降落設施下降 , 在那裡 , 太空梭會起飛和降落 。
and my partner byron lichtenberg and i carefully suspended him into zerog .	我和我的夥伴艾倫•利奇伯格和我小心地將他暫停為零 。
once he was there , [we] let him go to experience what weightlessness was truly like .	一旦他到那裡 , 讓他去體驗無重力是什麼樣子 。
and after that first parabola , you know , the doc said everything is great . he was smiling , and we said go .	在第一台降落傘之後 , 醫生說一切都很棒 。 他在微笑 , 我們說 , 開始吧 。
so we did a second parabola .	所以我們做了第二個拋物機 。
we actually floated an apple in homage to sir isaac newton because professor hawking holds the same chair at cambridge that isaac newton did .	實際上 , 我們在霍姆斯•牛頓的同一顆蘋果 , 因為霍金教授在劍橋的同一椅子 , 艾薩克•牛頓的確有同樣的椅子 。
and we did a fourth , and a fifth and a sixth .	我們做了第四個 , 第五個和第六個 。
and a seventh and an eighth .	第七次和第八次 。
and this man does not look like a 65yearold wheelchairbound man .	這位男士看起來不像65歲的輪椅男子 。
he was so happy .	他很開心 。
we are living on a precious jewel , and it's during our lifetime that we're moving off this planet .	我們活在一個珍貴的珠寶上 , 在我們一生中 , 我們就要離開這個星球 。
please join us in this epic adventure .	請加入我們這次史詩般的冒險 。
medical animator david bolinsky presents 3 minutes of stunning animation that show the bustling life inside a cell .	醫學動畫師大衛•布林斯基展示了3分鐘的驚人動畫 , 顯示細胞內的破裂性生命 。
design , entertainment , film , health , medicine , science , technology , visualizations	設計、娛樂、電影、健康、醫學、科學、技術、視覺化的視覺化 。
david bolinsky animates a cell	大衛•布林斯基將細胞動畫成細胞 。
i'm a medical illustrator , and i come from a slightly different point of view .	我是醫學插畫家 , 我來自一個稍微不同的觀點 。
i've been watching , since i grew up , the expressions of truth and beauty in the arts and truth and beauty in the sciences .	自從我長大以後 , 藝術和真理和美的表達 , 我一直都在看 , 在科學界的真相和美麗 。
and while these are both wonderful things in their own right they both have very wonderful things going for them truth and beauty as ideals that can be looked at by the sciences and by math are almost like the ideal conjoined twins that a scientist would want to date .	雖然這兩者都屬於他們自己的權利 , 他們都有非常美好的事物 , 讓他們成為理想和美麗 , 可以被科學和數學視為理想的雙胞胎 , 幾乎是科學家想要約會的理想雙胞胎 。
these are expressions of truth as awefull things , by meaning they are things you can worship .	這些表達真相是不可思議的 , 意思是 , 它們是你可以崇拜的事物 。
they are ideals that are powerful . they are irreducible .	它們是強大的理想 。 它們是不可思議的 。
they are unique . they are useful sometimes , often a long time after the fact .	它們是獨一無二的 , 有時它們是有用的 , 通常是經過事實的很長一段時間 。
and you can actually roll some of the pictures now , because i don't want to look at me on the screen .	你現在可以翻開一些照片 , 因為我不想在螢幕上看我 。
truth and beauty are things that are often opaque to people who are not in the sciences .	真相和美 , 通常對不在科學界的人來說是不相同的 。
they are things that describe beauty in a way that is often only accessible if you understand the language and the syntax of the person who studies the subject in which truth and beauty is expressed .	它們是描述美好的方式 , 通常只能了解語言和研究真相和美的說法 , 才會被表達 。
if you look at the math , e=mc squared , if you look at the cosmological constant , where there's an anthropic ideal , where you see that life had to evolve from the numbers that describe the universe these are things that are really difficult to understand .	如果你看數學 , e=mc平方 , 如果你看宇宙的常數 , 那裡有一個人類的理想 , 你會發現生命必須從描述宇宙的數字中演化 , 這些是很難理解的 。
and what i've tried to do since i had my training as a medical illustrator since i was taught animation by my father , who was a sculptor and my visual mentor i wanted to figure out a way to help people understand truth and beauty in the biological sciences by using animation , by using pictures , by telling stories so that the things that are not necessarily evident to people can be brought forth , and can be taught , and can be understood .	自從我受過醫學插畫師 , 自從我父親教導的醫學插畫師 , 也是我的視覺導師 , 我想要找出一種方法 , 協助人們了解生物科學的真相和美 , 透過動畫 , 透過動畫 , 說故事 , 那些不見得見的東西 , 不見得能被引來 , 且能被教導 , 且能被理解 , 且能被理解 。
students today are often immersed in an environment where what they learn is subjects that have truth and beauty embedded in them , but the way they're taught is compartmentalized and it's drawn down to the point where the truth and beauty are not always evident .	現今的學生經常沉浸在一個環境中 , 在那裡 , 他們所學到的主題是真和美的 , 但他們被教導的方式是比較化的 , 且它會被吸引到真實和美不見得見 。
it's almost like that old recipe for chicken soup where you boil the chicken until the flavor is just gone .	幾乎就像是雞湯的舊食譜 , 讓你把雞煮沸 , 直到香味消失 。
we don't want to do that to our students .	我們不想對我們的學生這樣做 。
so we have an opportunity to really open up education .	所以我們有機會真正打開教育 。
and i had a telephone call from robert lue at harvard , in the molecular and cellular biology department , a couple of years ago . he asked me if my team and i would be interested and willing to really change how medical and scientific education is done at harvard .	我接到哈佛大學的robertlue的電話 , 在分子和細胞生物學系中 , 幾年前 。 他問我 , 我的團隊是否有興趣 , 願意真正改變哈佛的醫學和科學教育是如何運作的 。
so we embarked on a project that would explore the cell that would explore the truth and beauty inherent in molecular and cellular biology so that students could understand a larger picture that they could hang all of these facts on .	因此我們開始進行一個探索細胞的項目 , 探索分子和細胞生物學的真相和美 , 讓學生能夠了解它們能夠懸掛這些事實的大圖片 。
they could have a mental image of the cell as a large , bustling , hugely complicated city that's occupied by micromachines .	他們可能有像細胞一樣大、很忙碌、非常複雜的城市 , 被微機械所佔據 。
and these micromachines really are at the heart of life .	而這些微機械其實是生命的核心 。
these micromachines , which are the envy of nanotechnologists the world over , are selfdirected , powerful , precise , accurate devices that are made out of strings of amino acids .	這些微機械 , 是世界各地的奈米科技專家 , 自給自足、強大、精確、精確的裝置 , 由胺基酸所組成 。
and these micromachines power how a cell moves .	而這些微機械能驅動細胞如何移動 。
they power how a cell replicates . they power our hearts .	它們驅動細胞如何複製 。 它們驅動我們的心 。
they power our minds .	它們驅使我們的心靈 。
and so what we wanted to do was to figure out how we could make this story into an animation that would be the centerpiece of biovisions at harvard , which is a website that harvard has for its molecular and cellular biology students that will in addition to all the textual information , in addition to all the didactic stuff put everything together visually , so that these students would have an internalized view of what a cell really is in all of its truth and beauty , and be able to study with this view in mind , so that their imaginations would be sparked , so that their passions would be sparked and so that they would be able to go on and use these visions in their head to make new discoveries and to be able to find out , really , how life works .	所以 , 我們想做的是 , 想辦法把這個故事變成一個動畫 , 讓這個故事成為哈佛生物的中心中心 , 一個網站 , 哈佛對它的分子和細胞生物學的學生 , 除了所有的文字信息 , 除了所有文字信息 , 視覺上來說 , 這些學生對於細胞的真實和美麗的看法 , 並能夠研究它們的想像力 , 以致於它們的速度傳播出去 。
so we set out by looking at how these molecules are put together .	所以我們開始研究這些分子是如何組合在一起的 。
we worked with a theme , which is , you've got macrophages that are streaming down a capillary , and they're touching the surface of the capillary wall , and they're picking up information from cells that are on the capillary wall , and they are given this information that there's an inflammation somewhere outside , where they can't see and sense .	我們和一個主題合作 , 也就是說 , 你有大腸桿菌 , 它們會觸碰毛細菌的表面 , 它們會從毛細菌牆上撿取資訊 , 它們會給外部的發炎信息 , 在那裡 , 牠們看不見和知覺 。
but they get the information that causes them to stop , causes them to internalize that they need to make all of the various parts that will cause them to change their shape , and try to get out of this capillary and find out what's going on .	但他們得到使他們停下來的信息 , 使他們內化 , 他們需要製造所有會造成改變形狀的零件 , 試著脫離這個毛細節 , 找出發生了什麼事 。
so these molecular motors we had to work with the harvard scientists and databank models of the atomically accurate molecules and figure out how they moved , and figure out what they did .	所以這些分子馬達我們必須和哈佛科學家和資料庫的模型合作 , 找出它們如何移動 , 找出它們的作用 。
and figure out how to do this in a way that was truthful in that it imparted what was going on , but not so truthful that the compact crowding in a cell would prevent the vista from happening .	要知道如何用真誠的方式來做這件事 , 讓它隱含了發生了什麼事 , 但不太誠實 , 細胞內的結合會阻止惡作劇發生 。
and so what i'm going to show you is a threeminute reader's digest version of the first aspect of this film that we produced . it's an ongoing project that's going to go another four or five years .	接下來我要給大家看的是一個三分鐘的讀者的消化版本 , 是我們製作的這部影片的第一面 。 這是一個持續進行的計畫 , 四到五年 。
and i want you to look at this and see the paths that the cell manufactures these little walking machines , they're called kinesins that take these huge loads that would challenge an ant in relative size .	請各位看看這個 , 看看細胞製造這些小步行機器的路徑 , 它們被稱作 「 鹼基 」 , 將這些龐大的負荷 , 以相對大小來挑戰螞蟻的大小 。
run the movie , please .	請播放這部電影 。
but these machines that power the inside of the cells are really quite amazing , and they really are the basis of all life because all of these machines interact with each other .	但這些機器在細胞內部發電非常驚人 , 它們真的是所有生命的基礎 , 因為這些機器彼此互動 。
they pass information to each other .	它們會把資訊傳給彼此 。
they cause different things to happen inside the cell .	它們會造成不同的事情發生在細胞內 。
and the cell will actually manufacture the parts that it needs on the fly , from information that's brought from the nucleus by molecules that read the genes .	細胞會將果蠅所需的部分製造出來 , 透過讀取基因的分子所得到的資訊 。
no life , from the smallest life to everybody here , would be possible without these little micromachines .	沒有生命 , 從最小的生命到這裡的每一個人 , 沒有這些微機械 。
in fact , it would really , in the absence of these machines , have made the attendance here , chris , really quite sparse .	事實上 , 真的 , 在沒有這些機器的情況下 , 克里斯 , 非常矛盾 。
this is the fedex delivery guy of the cell .	這是細胞的fedex外送傢伙 。
this little guy is called the kinesin , and he pulls a sack that's full of brand new manufactured proteins to wherever it's needed in the cell whether it's to a membrane , whether it's to an organelle , whether it's to build something or repair something .	這個小傢伙叫做kinesin , 他拉著一堆全新的製造蛋白質 , 到細胞需要的位置 , 不論是細胞膜 , 不論是器官 , 不論是用來製造東西或修復東西 。
and each of us has about 100 , 000 of these things running around , right now , inside each one of your 100 trillion cells .	我們每一個人都有大約十萬個這種東西跑來跑去 , 就在你100兆個細胞中 。
so no matter how lazy you feel , you're not really intrinsically doing nothing .	所以 , 不論你有多懶惰 , 你根本不做任何事 。
so what i want you to do when you go home is think about this , and think about how powerful our cells are .	所以 , 當你回家時 , 我希望你能想一想 , 想想我們的細胞有多強大 。
and think about some of the things that we're learning about cellular mechanics .	想想我們所學到的一些關於細胞機械的東西 。
once we figure out all that's going on and believe me , we know almost a percent of what's going on once we figure out what's going on , we're really going to be able to have a lot of control over what we do with our health , with what we do with future generations , and how long we're going to live .	一旦我們了解了一切 , 相信我 , 我們幾乎知道發生了什麼事 , 一旦我們知道發生了什麼事 , 我們就真的能夠掌控我們對我們的健康和未來的世代所做的事 , 以及我們將要活多久 。
and hopefully we'll be able to use this to discover more truth , and more beauty .	希望我們能用它來發現更多的真相 , 更美麗 。
but it's really quite amazing that these cells , these micromachines , are aware enough of what the cell needs that they do their bidding .	但很驚人的是 , 這些細胞 , 這些微機械 , 已經知道它們所需要的細胞需要什麼 。
they work together . they make the cell do what it needs to do .	它們一起工作 , 讓細胞做它要做的事 。
and their working together helps our bodies huge entities that they will never see function properly .	他們一起工作 , 協助我們身體的巨大實體 , 它們永遠看不見功能 。
enjoy the rest of the show . thank you .	享受剩下的節目 。 謝謝 。
becky blanton planned to live in her van for a year and see the country , but when depression set in and her freelance job ended , her camping trip turned into homelessness . in this intimate talk , she describes her experience of becoming one of america's working homeless .	貝琪•布蘭頓計畫要在她的車中住一年 , 去看這個國家 , 但當憂鬱和她的自由工作結束時 , 她的營運變成無家可歸的旅程 。 在這個親密的演講中 , 她描述了成為美國的無家可歸 。
adventure , happiness , life , personal growth , poverty , social change , society , storytelling	冒險、幸福、生活、個人成長、貧窮、社會變遷、社會、說故事、說故事、說故事、說故事 。
becky blanton: the year i was homeless	貝琪•布蘭頓:那年我無家可歸 , 無家可歸 。
i'm a writer and a journalist , and i'm also an insanely curious person , so in 22 years as a journalist , i've learned how to do a lot of new things .	我是作家和記者 , 我也是個瘋狂的好奇人 , 所以22年來 , 身為記者 , 我學會了如何做很多新事 。
and three years ago , one of the things i learned how to do was to become invisible .	三年前 , 我學到的其中一件事就是成為隱形人 。
i became one of the working homeless .	我成為了無家可歸的無家可歸者 。
i quit my job as a newspaper editor after my father died in february of that same year , and decided to travel .	同年二月 , 我辭去了報紙編輯工作 , 決定去旅行 。
his death hit me pretty hard .	他的死亡讓我非常難受 。
and there were a lot of things that i wanted to feel and deal with while i was doing that .	當我在做這件事時 , 我有很多想感受和處理的事情 。
i've camped my whole life . and i decided that living in a van for a year to do this would be like one long camping trip .	我一生都在幫忙 。 我決定 , 住在一輛車裡 , 住了一趟旅程 , 大概是一趟漫長的營地旅行 。
so i packed my cat , my rottweiler and my camping gear into a 1975 chevy van , and drove off into the sunset , having fully failed to realize three critical things .	我把我的貓打包 , 我和rotweiler和我的營地裝在1975年的清潔車上 , 開車進入日落 , 完全沒有意識到三件重要的事 。
one: that society equates living in a permanent structure , even a shack , with having value as a person .	第一:社會等於生活在一個永久的結構中 , 甚至是一塊垃圾 , 身為一個人 。
two: i failed to realize how quickly the negative perceptions of other people can impact our reality , if we let it .	第二:我沒有意識到 , 別人的負面感知有多快 , 會影響我們的現實 , 如果我們放下它 。
three: i failed to realize that homelessness is an attitude , not a lifestyle .	第三:我沒有意識到 , 無家可歸是一種態度 , 而不是生活方式 。
at first , living in the van was great .	一開始 , 住在車內是很棒的 。
i showered in campgrounds . i ate out regularly .	我在營地上洗澡 。 我常常吃東西 。
and i had time to relax and to grieve .	我有時間放鬆和悲慟 。
but then the anger and the depression about my father's death set in .	但接著 , 關於我父親死亡的憤怒和憂鬱 。
my freelance job ended . and i had to get a fulltime job to pay the bills .	我的自由工作終結了 。 我得要全職工作才能支付帳單 。
what had been a really mild spring turned into a miserably hot summer .	一個非常溫和的春天變成一個悲慘的炎熱夏天 。
and it became impossible to park anywhere without being very obvious that i had a cat and a dog with me , and it was really hot .	任何地方的公園都沒明顯 , 我有一隻貓和一隻狗 , 真的很熱 。
the cat came and went through an open window in the van .	貓來了 , 穿過車子的開窗 。
the doggy went into doggy day care .	小狗就照顧了小狗 。
whenever i could , i used employee showers in office buildings and truck stops .	每當我可以 , 我都會用辦公大樓的員工淋浴 , 卡車停下來 。
or i washed up in public rest rooms .	或我在公共場所清洗 。
nighttime temperatures in the van rarely dropped below 80 degrees fahrenheit , making it difficult or impossible to sleep .	夜間車廂的溫度很少在華氏80度下降 , 讓它很難或無法入眠 。
food rotted in the heat .	食物在熱中旋轉 。
ice in my ice chest melted within hours , and it was pretty miserable .	冰裡的冰會在幾小時內融化 , 非常悲慘 。
i couldn't afford to find an apartment , or couldn't afford an apartment that would allow me to have the rottweiler and the cat .	我買不起公寓 , 或買不起一間公寓 , 讓我有rotweiler和貓 。
and i refused to give them up , so i stayed in the van .	我拒絕放棄他們 , 所以我留在車裡 。
and when the heat made me too sick to walk the 50 feet to the public restroom outside my van at night , i used a bucket and a trash bag as a toilet .	當熱使我太生病了 , 我晚上在車外走50英尺的公共廁所時 , 我用一個桶子和一個垃圾袋作為廁所 。
when winter weather set in , the temperatures dropped below freezing . and they stayed there .	當冬天進來時 , 溫度降低在冰凍之下 , 溫度就在那兒 。
and i faced a whole new set of challenges .	我面對了一套全新的挑戰 。
i parked a different place every night so i would avoid being noticed and hassled by the police .	我每天晚上停下一個不同的地方 , 以免被警察察察逮捕 , 被警察逮捕 。
i didn't always succeed .	我並不總是成功的 。
but i felt out of control of my life .	但我覺得我無法掌控我的人生 。
and i don't know when or how it happened , but the speed at which i went from being a talented writer and journalist to being a homeless woman , living in a van , took my breath away .	我不知道發生了什麼事 , 但是我從一個有才華的作家和記者 , 變成一個無家可歸的女人 , 把我的呼吸帶走了 。
i hadn't changed . my i . q . hadn't dropped .	我還沒改變 , 我的智商並沒有下降 。
my talent , my integrity , my values , everything about me remained the same .	我的才華 , 我的正直 , 我的價值觀 , 所有關於我的事都一樣 。
but i had changed somehow .	但我不知怎麼地改變了 。
i spiraled deeper and deeper into a depression .	我更深入地陷入了憂鬱症 。
and eventually someone referred me to a homeless health clinic .	最後有人把我稱為無家可歸的健康診所 。
and i went . i hadn't bathed in three days .	我去了 , 三天後我還沒洗澡 。
i was as smelly and as depressed as anyone in line .	我就像在排隊中的任何人一樣 , 感到沮喪 。
i just wasn't drunk or high .	我只是不喝醉或喝醉 。
and when several of the homeless men realized that , including a former university professor , they said , " you aren't homeless . why are you really here ? "	當數位無家可歸的男士意識到 , 包括前大學教授 , 他們說: 「 你不是無家可歸的 。 為什麼你真的在這裡 ? 」
other homeless people didn't see me as homeless , but i did .	其他無家可歸的人並沒有把我視為無家可歸的人 , 但我確實這麼做了 。
then the professor listened to my story and he said , " you have a job . you have hope .	接著 , 教授聽我的故事 , 他說: 「 你有工作 , 你有希望 。
the real homeless don't have hope . "	真正的無家可歸者沒有希望 。 」
a reaction to the medication the clinic gave me for my depression left me suicidal . and i remember thinking , " if i killed myself , no one would notice . "	診所的反應是 , 診所給我的憂鬱症 , 讓我自殺了 。 我記得我在想: 「 如果我殺了自己 , 沒有人會注意到 。 」
a friend told me , shortly after that , that she had heard that tim russert , a nationally renowned journalist , had been talking about me on national t . v .	不久後 , 一位朋友告訴我 , 她聽說提姆•魯斯特 , 一個全國知名的記者 , 一直在談論我在國家電視台上 。
an essay i'd written about my father , the year before he died , was in tim's new book .	我寫了一篇關於我父親的文章 , 在他死前的那一年 , 提姆的新書 。
and he was doing the talk show circuit . and he was talking about my writing .	他在做這場演說的電路 。 他在談我的寫作 。
and when i realized that tim russert , former moderator of " meet the press , " was talking about my writing , while i was living in a van in a walmart parking lot , i started laughing .	當我意識到提姆•魯斯特 , 《會見媒體》的前主持人談到我的寫作 , 當我住在華爾瑪停車場時 , 我開始笑 。
i started laughing because it got to the point where , was i a writer , or was i a homeless woman ?	我開始笑是因為我是作家 , 還是我是無家可歸的女人 ?
so i went in the bookstore . and i found tim's book .	於是我走進書店 , 找到提姆的書 。
and i stood there . and i reread my essay .	我站在那裡 , 我重寫我的文章 。
because i was a writer .	因為我是個作家 。
i was a writer .	我是個作家 。
shortly after that i moved back to tennessee .	在那之後不久我搬回田納西 。
i alternated between living in a van and couch surfing with friends .	我和朋友住在車內的沙發和沙發衝浪中間 。
and i started writing again .	我又開始寫作了 。
by the summer of the following year i was a working journalist .	隔年夏天 , 我是一位職業記者 。
i was winning awards . i was living in my own apartment .	我贏了獎 , 我住在我自己的公寓裡 。
i was no longer homeless .	我不再無家可歸 。
and i was no longer invisible .	我不再隱形了 。
thousands of people work full and parttime jobs , and live in their cars .	數以千計的人全職工作 , 生活在他們的車上 。
but society continues to stigmatize and criminalize living in your vehicle or on the streets .	但社會持續汙名化和罪犯生活在你的車或街道上 。
so the homeless , the working homeless , primarily remain invisible .	所以 , 無家可歸的無家可歸 , 主要是隱形 。
but if you ever meet one , engage them , encourage them , and offer them hope .	但如果你曾經遇過一個 , 參與他們 , 鼓勵他們 , 並提供他們希望 。
the human spirit can overcome anything if it has hope .	如果有希望 , 人類的精神就能克服任何事情 。
and i'm not here to be the poster girl for the homeless .	我不是來這裡成為無家可歸的海報 。
i'm not here to encourage you to give money to the next panhandler you meet .	我不是要鼓勵你們把錢給你下一個乞討者 。
but i am here to tell you that , based on my experience , people are not where they live , where they sleep , or what their life situation is at any given time .	但我在這裡要告訴各位 , 根據我的經驗 , 人們不是他們住的地方 , 他們睡在哪裡 , 或是他們任何時間的情境 。
three years ago i was living in a van in a walmart parking lot , and today i'm speaking at ted .	三年前 , 我住在華爾瑪停車場 , 今天我在ted演講 。
hope always , always finds a way . thank you .	希望永遠都能找到方法 。 謝謝 。
at tedxchange , thailand's " mr . condom , " mechai viravaidya , walks us through the country's bold plan to raise its standard of living , starting in the 1970s . first step: population control . and that means a lot of frank , funny and very effective talk about condoms .	在tedxchange , 泰國的 " 保險套先生 " mechaiviraida , 帶領我們走遍全國大膽的計劃從1970年代開始 , 第一步是人口控制 , 這意味著許多法蘭克 , 非常有趣和有效的談保險套 。
culture , global issues , health , population , science	文化、全球議題、健康、人口、科學、科學、科學、科學、科學議題、 。
mechai viravaidya: how mr . condom made thailand a better place	麥卡伊•維瓦伊亞:保險套如何讓泰國成為更好的地方 , 泰國先生:保險套如何讓泰國成為更好的地方 。
now , when i was a young man 40 years ago , the country was very , very poor with lots and lots and lots of people living in poverty .	四十年前 , 當我還是個年輕人的時候 , 這個國家非常非常貧窮 , 有許多人住在貧窮 。
we decided to do something about it , but we didn't begin with a welfare program or a poverty reduction program .	我們決定為此做點什麼 , 但我們並沒有從福利計畫開始 , 或減少貧窮計畫 。
but we began with a familyplanning program , following a very successful maternal child health activity , sets of activities .	但我們從家庭平台開始 , 遵循一個非常成功的孕產兒健康活動 , 一組活動 。
so basically , no one would accept family planning if their children didn't survive .	基本上 , 沒有人能接受家庭規劃 , 如果他們的孩子沒有存活下來 ,
so the first step: get to the children , get to the mothers , and then follow up with family planning .	第一步:送到孩子們 , 送到母親去 , 然後跟隨家人的計劃 。
not just child mortality alone , you need also family planning .	不僅僅是兒童死亡率 , 你還需要家庭規劃 。
now let me take you back as to why we needed to do it .	現在 , 讓我帶各位回到為何我們需要這麼做 。
in my country , that was the case in 1974 .	在我的國家 , 那是1974年的情況 。
seven children per family tremendous growth at 3 . 3 percent .	每個家庭的七個孩子 , 成長率高達3.3% 。
there was just no future .	沒有未來 。
we needed to reduce the population growth rate .	我們需要降低人口成長率 。
so we said , " let's do it . "	所以我們說: 「 我們來做吧 。 」
the women said , " we agree . we'll use pills , but we need a doctor to prescribe the pills , " and we had very , very few doctors .	女性說: 「 我們同意 。 我們會用藥 , 但我們需要醫生來開藥 , 」 我們有非常非常少的醫生 。
we didn't take no as an answer ; we took no as a question .	我們沒有接受答案 , 我們把不當作一個問題 。
we went to the nurses and the midwives , who were also women , and did a fantastic job at explaining how to use the pill .	我們去了護士和助產士 , 他們也是女人 , 做了一個很棒的工作 , 解釋如何用藥 。
that was wonderful , but it covered only 20 percent of the country .	這很棒 , 但它只佔了全國的20% 。
what do we do for the other 80 percent leave them alone and say , " well , they're not medical personnel . "	我們為其他百分之八十的人做些什麼 , 讓他們獨自說: 「 嗯 , 他們不是醫療人員 。 」
no , we decided to do a bit more .	不 , 我們決定多做一點 。
so we went to the ordinary people that you saw .	所以我們去看你看到的一般人 。
actually , below that yellow sign i wish they hadn't wiped that , because there was " cocacola " there .	事實上 , 在那黃色標誌之下 , 我希望他們還沒聽過這個 , 因為那裡有 「 可口可樂 」 。
we were so much bigger than cocacola in those days .	當時我們比可口可樂大很多 。
and no difference , the people they chose were the people we chose .	沒有差別 , 他們選的就是我們選的人 。
they were wellknown in the community , they knew that customers were always right , and they were terrific , and they practiced their family planning themselves .	他們在社區中很著名 , 他們知道客戶總是對的 , 他們很棒 , 他們也很棒 , 他們練習了他們的家庭規劃 。
so they could supply pills and condoms throughout the country , in every village of the country .	所以他們可以在全國各地供應藥品和保險套 , 在每個村落都有 。
so there we are . we went to the people who were seen as the cause of the problem to be the solution .	所以 , 我們就在那裡 。 我們去找那些被視為是問題的成因 。
wherever there were people and you can see boats with the women , selling things here's the floating market selling bananas and crabs and also contraceptives wherever you find people , you'll find contraceptives in thailand .	不論在哪裡 , 都有人 , 你都可以看到有女性的船 , 賣東西是漂浮市場 , 賣香蕉和螃蟹 , 不論你在泰國找到人 , 你都會在泰國找到避孕工具 。
and then we decided , why not get to religion because in the philippines , the catholic church was pretty strong , and thai people were buddhist .	然後我們決定 , 為什麼不上宗教 , 因為在菲律賓 , 天主教會很強壯 , 泰國人是佛教徒 。
we went to them and they said , " look , could you help us ? "	我們去找他們 , 他們說: 「 你能幫我們嗎 ? 」
i'm there the one in blue , not the yellow holding a bowl of holy water for the monk to sprinkle holy water on pills and condoms for the sanctity of the family .	我在那裡是藍色的 , 不是黃色 , 拿著一碗聖水 , 讓僧侶能在藥丸和保險套上灑水 。
and this picture was sent throughout the country .	這張照片遍佈全國 。
so some of the monks in the villages were doing the same thing themselves .	所以 , 村落中的一些僧侶正在自己做同樣的事 。
and the women were saying , " no wonder we have no sideeffects .	女人說: 「 難怪我們沒有副作用 。
it's been blessed . "	它被祝福了 。 」
that was their perception .	那是他們的感知 。
and then we went to teachers .	然後我們去了教師 。
you need everybody to be involved in trying to provide whatever it is that make humanity a better place .	你需要每一個人試著提供任何東西 , 讓人類成為一個更好的地方 。
so we went to the teachers .	所以我們去了教師 。
over a quarter of a million were taught about family planning with a new alphabet a , b for birth , c for condom , i for iud , v for vasectomy .	超過25萬人被教導要用一個新的字母a、b出生、保險套、iud、v等級 。
and then we had a snakes and ladders game , where you throw dice .	然後我們就有了蛇和梯子遊戲 , 你丟了骰子 。
if you land on anything profamily planning , you move ahead .	如果你登陸任何熟悉的計劃 , 你就會向前移動 。
like , " mother takes the pill every night .	例如: 「 媽媽每晚都會吃藥 。
very good , mother . move ahead .	非常好 , 媽媽 , 向前走 。
uncle buys a condom . very good , uncle . move ahead .	叔叔買保險套 , 非常好 , 叔叔 。 向前走 。
uncle gets drunk , doesn't use condom . come back , start again . "	叔叔喝醉 , 不用保險套 , 回來 , 再回來吧 。 」
again , education , class entertainment .	同樣的 , 教育、娛樂 。
and the kids were doing it in school too .	孩子們也在學校做這件事 。
we had relay races with condoms , we had children's condomblowing championship .	我們和保險套有相關的種族 , 我們有兒童保險套冠軍 。
and before long , the condom was know as the girl's best friend .	不久前 , 保險套被稱為 「 女孩最好的朋友 」 。
in thailand , for poor people , diamonds don't make it so the condom is the girl's best friend .	在泰國 , 對窮人來說 , 鑽石不會製造 , 所以保險套是女孩最好的朋友 。
we introduced our first microcredit program in 1975 , and the women who organized it said , " we only want to lend to women who practice family planning .	我們在1975年推出了第一項微型貸款計畫 , 組織它的婦女說: 「 我們只想借用那些實踐家庭規劃的女性 。
if you're pregnant , take care of your pregnancy .	如果你懷孕了 , 照顧你的懷孕 。
if you're not pregnant , you can take a loan out from us . "	如果你不懷孕 , 你可以從我們身上拿出貸款 。 」
and that was run by them .	那是他們經營的 。
and after 35/36 years , it's still going on .	在35/36年之後 , 它仍然持續下去 。
it's a part of the village development bank ; it's not a real bank , but it's a fund microcredit .	它是村落發展銀行的一部分 , 不是真的銀行 , 而是一個基礎小額貸款 。
and we didn't need a big organization to run it it was run by the villagers themselves .	我們不需要一個大型組織來經營它 , 由村民自己經營 。
and you probably hardly see a thai man there , it's always women , women , women , women .	你可能幾乎看不到泰國男子 , 總是女性、女性、女性、女性 。
and then we thought we'd help america , because america's been helping everyone , whether they want help or not .	然後我們以為我們會幫助美國 , 因為美國一直在幫助所有人 , 不論他們是否想要幫助 。
and this is on the fourth of july .	這是7月4日 。
we decided to provide vasectomy to all men , but in particular , american men to the front of the queue , right up to the ambassador's residence during his [unclear] .	我們決定為所有男人提供遠方的機會 , 但特別是 , 美國人在排隊前面 , 直接到大使館的居民 。
and the hotel gave us the ballroom for it very appropriate room .	旅館給了我們一個球場 , 給了我們一個非常適合的房間 。
and since it was near lunch time , they said , " all right , we'll give you some lunch .	既然是近午餐時間 , 他們說: 「 好吧 , 我們會給你午餐 。
of course , it must be american cola .	當然 , 這一定是美國的可口可樂 。
you get two brands , coke and pepsi .	你有兩個品牌、可口可樂和百事可樂 。
and then the food is either hamburger or hotdog . "	食物不是漢堡或熱狗 。 」
and i thought a hotdog will be more symbolic .	我以為熱狗會更具象徵性 。
and here is this , then , young man called willy bohm who worked for the usaid .	這裡是這個 , 名叫威利•博姆的年輕人 , 他為美國人工作 。
obviously , he's had his vasectomy because his hotdog is half eaten , and he was very happy .	很顯然 , 他有他的遠方 , 因為他的熱狗吃了一半 , 他非常開心 。
it made a lot of news in america , and it angered some people also .	它在美國有很多消息 , 有些人也很憤怒 。
i said , " don't worry . come over and i'll do the whole lot of you . "	我說: 「 別擔心 , 過來 , 我會幫你們做一整件事 。 」
in all this thing , from seven children to 1 . 5 children , population growth rate of 3 . 3 to 0 . 5 .	總而言之 , 從七個孩子到1.5個孩子 , 人口成長率是3.3到0.5 。

but it's everybody's job who can change attitude and behavior .	但每個人都能改變態度和行為 。
then aids came along and hit thailand , and we had to stop doing a lot of good things to fight aids .	接著 , 愛滋病來到泰國 , 我們得要停止對抗愛滋病的好事 。

so i thought , " well , if you can't go to the government , go to the military . "	所以我想: 「 嗯 , 如果你不去政府 , 去軍隊 。 」
so i went to the military and asked to borrow 300 radio stations .	所以我去了軍隊 , 請我借了300台無線電站 。
they have more than the government , and they've got more guns than the government .	他們比政府還多 , 他們的槍枝比政府多 。
so i asked them , could they help us in our fight against hiv .	所以我問他們 , 他們能否協助我們對抗愛滋病毒 。
and after i gave them statistics , they said , " yes . okay . you can use all the radio stations , television stations . "	在我給他們統計數據之後 , 他們說: 「 好 , 你可以用所有的電台 , 電視站 。 」
and that's when we went onto the airwaves .	那時我們進入了空中 。

he became the chairman of the national aids committee and increased the budget fiftyfold .	他成為了全國愛滋病委員會的主席 , 增加預算的五十倍 。
every ministry , even judges , had to be involved in aids education everyone and we said the public , institutions , religious institutions , schools everyone was involved .	每一個部長 , 甚至法官 , 都得參與愛滋病教育 , 我們說公眾、機構、宗教機構 , 所有人都參與過學校 。
and here , every media person had to be trained for hiv .	在這裡 , 每一位媒體人員都得受過愛滋病的訓練 。
and we gave every station half a minute extra for advertising to earn more money .	我們給每一站五分鐘額外的廣告 , 來賺更多錢 。
so they were happy with that .	所以他們對此感到滿意 。
and then aids education in all schools , starting from university .	接著 , 所有學校都有愛滋病教育 , 從大學開始 。
and these are high school kids teaching high school kids .	這些是高中生教高中生 。
and the best teachers were the girls , not the boys , and they were terrific .	最好的老師是女孩 , 不是男孩 , 他們很棒 。
and these girls who go around teaching about safe sex and hiv were known as mother theresa .	這些在教導安全性愛和愛滋病毒的女孩 , 被稱為 「 母親 」 。
and then we went down one more step .	然後我們再走下一步 。
these are primary school kids third , fourth grade going to every household in the village , every household in the whole of thailand , giving aids information and a condom to every household , given by these young kids .	這些是主要的學校孩子第三年級 , 四年級到村子裡的每個家庭 , 每個家庭都在泰國 , 提供愛滋病資訊和保險套給每個家庭 , 給這些孩子 。

and they loved him . you need a symbol of something .	他們很愛他 , 你需要一個象徵 。
in every country , every program , you need a symbol , and this is probably the best thing he's ever done with his mba .	在每個國家 , 每個計畫 , 你都需要一個象徵 , 這可能是他在mba所做過最好的事情 。
and then we gave condoms out everywhere on the streets everywhere , everywhere .	然後我們在街上隨處可見的保險套 。

and also , in traffic , the policemen give you condoms our " cops and rubbers " programs .	此外 , 警方也給了你保險套 , 我們的 「 警察 」 和 「 橡膠 」 計畫 。

we had condoms in all the refrigerators in the hotels and the schools , because alcohol impairs judgment .	我們在飯店和學校裡都有保險套 , 因為酒精會損壞評斷 。

because poor people are business people who lack business skills and access to credit .	因為窮人是商人 , 他們缺乏商業技能和取得功勞 。
those are the things to be provided by the business community .	這些是商業界提供的服務 。
we're trying to turn them into barefoot entrepreneurs , little business people .	我們試著把他們變成赤腳企業家 , 小商人 。
the only way out of poverty is through business enterprise .	脫貧的唯一方法是經營企業 。
so , that was done .	所以 , 完成了 。
the money goes from the company into the village via treeplanting .	公司的錢從公司轉變成村莊 , 透過樹木移植 。
it's not a free gift .	這不是免費禮物 。
they plant the trees , and the money goes into their microcredit fund , which we call the village development bank .	他們種植樹木 , 金錢會進入他們的微額貸款基金 , 我們稱之為 「 村落發展銀行 」 。
everybody joins in , and they feel they own the bank , because they have brought the money in .	每個人都加入 , 他們覺得自己擁有銀行 , 因為他們把錢帶進來 。
and before you can borrow the money , you need to be trained .	在你借錢之前 , 你需要被訓練 。
and we believe if you want to help the poor , those who are living in poverty , access to credit must be a human right .	我們相信如果你想幫助窮人 , 住在貧窮的人 , 信用肯定是人權 。
access to credit must be a human right .	信用法一定是人權 。
otherwise they'll never get out of poverty .	否則他們永遠不會脫離貧窮 。
and then before getting a loan , you must be trained .	在取得貸款之前 , 你一定受過訓練 。
here's what we call a " barefoot mba , " teaching people how to do business so that , when they borrow money , they'll succeed with the business .	我們稱之為 「 赤腳mba 」 , 教導人們如何做生意 , 這樣一來 , 當他們借錢時 , 他們就會成功地做生意 。

they said , " they should stop making shoes and clothes .	他們說: 「 他們應該停止做鞋子和衣服 。
make these better , because we can afford them . "	讓這些東西變得更好 , 因為我們能負擔得起 。 」

so anyone sitting in and watching tv , get in touch with me .	任何人坐進去看電視 , 跟我聯絡 。

and then now , finally in education , we want to change the school as being underutilized into a place where it's a lifelong learning center for everyone .	最後 , 在教育方面 , 我們希望改變學校 , 成為一個地方 , 讓每個人終身學習中心 。

your smartphone may feel like a friend but a true friend would give you a smile once in a while . at ted2013 , keller rinaudo demos romo , the smartphonepowered mini robot who can motor along with you on a walk , slide you a cup of coffee across the table , and react to you with programmable expressions .	你的智慧手機可能會覺得好像朋友但真的朋友會給你微笑一陣子 。 在ted2013年 , 凱爾•里納多•羅摩 , 智慧型手機驅動小型機器人 , 可以在散步 , 滑行 , 滑行一杯咖啡橫跨桌 , 和你做出可程序表達的表達 。
keller rinaudo: a mini robot powered by your phone	kellerrinauuudo:一台迷你機器人是由你的手機發電的小型機器人所發電 。
so just by a show of hands , how many of you all have a robot at home ?	請舉手看 , 在座有多少人家裡有機器人 ?
not very many of you .	不是很多人 。
okay . and actually of those hands , if you don't include roomba how many of you have a robot at home ?	好吧 。 實際上 , 如果你不把機器人納入sorba , 你們當中有多少人在家裡有機器人 ?
that's the problem that we're trying to solve at romotive that i and the other 20 nerds at romotive are obsessed with solving .	這就是我們正在嘗試解決我和其他二十個角色角色角色角色的怪胎 , 迷上了解決問題 。
so we really want to build a robot that anyone can use , whether you're eight or 80 .	所以 , 我們真的想建立一個人都可以使用的機器人 , 不論你是八、八十歲 。
and as it turns out , that's a really hard problem , because you have to build a small , portable robot that's not only really affordable , but it has to be something that people actually want to take home and have around their kids .	結果發現 , 這真的是個很困難的問題 , 因為你要建立一個小型、可攜式的機器人 , 不只能負擔得起 , 它必須是人們真的想要帶回家 , 周圍有孩子 。
this robot can't be creepy or uncanny .	這種機器人不能是尖銳或不可思議 。
he should be friendly and cute .	他應該是友善且可愛的 。
romo's a robot that uses a device you already know and love your iphone as his brain .	romo的機器人 , 用了你已經知道且愛你的iphone , 來當作他的大腦 。
and by leveraging the power of the iphone's processor , we can create a robot that is wifi enabled and computer visioncapable for 150 bucks , which is about one percent of what these kinds of robots have cost in the past .	藉由控制iphone處理器的力量 , 我們就能創造一個可以用wi-fi的機器人 , 用於150塊美金的電腦視力 , 這大約是過去這類機器人所花費的百分之一 。
when romo wakes up , he's in creature mode .	當romo醒來時 , 他在生物模式中 。
so he's actually using the video camera on the device to follow my face .	所以他實際上是用這個攝影機在儀器上跟著我的臉 。
if i duck down , he'll follow me .	如果我失敗了 , 他會跟著我 。
he's wary , so he'll keep his eyes on me .	他很溫暖 , 所以他會盯著我看 。
if i come over here , he'll turn to follow me .	如果我來到這裡 , 他會轉向跟著我 。
if i come over here he's smart .	如果我來這裡 , 他很聰明 。
and if i get too close to him , he gets scared just like any other creature .	如果我太靠近他 , 他就跟其他生物一樣害怕 。
so in a lot of ways , romo is like a pet that has a mind of his own .	所以 , 在很多方面 , romo就像寵物一樣 , 他有自己的心智 。
thanks , little guy .	謝謝 , 小傢伙 。
and if i want to explore the world uhoh , romo's tired if i want to explore the world with romo , i can actually connect him from any other ios device .	如果我想要探索這個世界 , 嗯 , 如果我想要用romo來探索這個世界 , 我真的可以從任何ios裝置上連結他 。
so here's the ipad .	這是ipad 。
and romo will actually stream video to this device .	而romo會把視頻傳送給這個裝置 。

so i'll show you really quickly , romo actually he's streaming video , so you can see me and the entire ted audience .	我很快地給大家看romo實際上他在播放影片 , 各位可以看到我和整個ted觀眾 。
if i get in front of romo here .	如果我站在romo前面 。
and if i want to control him , i can just drive .	如果我想要控制他 , 我可以開車 。
