now grid cells are found , again , on the inputs to the hippocampus , and they're a bit like place cells .	此外 , 網格細胞又被輸入海馬體 , 它們有點像位置細胞 。
but now as the rat explores around , each individual cell fires in a whole array of different locations which are laid out across the environment in an amazingly regular triangular grid .	但當老鼠四處探索時 , 每個細胞都在一系列不同的位置 , 在一個非常規律的三角形格子中釋放出來 。
and if you record from several grid cells shown here in different colors each one has a gridlike firing pattern across the environment , and each cell's gridlike firing pattern is shifted slightly relative to the other cells .	如果你從幾個格子細胞中記錄下來 , 每一種顏色都有類似的連結模式 , 每一種細胞的發射模式會稍微改變與其他細胞的不同 。
so the red one fires on this grid and the green one on this one and the blue on on this one .	紅色的 , 紅色的 , 是這條線上的綠色螢幕 , 藍色在這個網格上 。
so together , it's as if the rat can put a virtual grid of firing locations across its environment a bit like the latitude and longitude lines that you'd find on a map , but using triangles .	總之 , 老鼠可以把虛擬的位置放到周圍的環境中 , 有點像你在地圖上看到的緯度和長距離 , 但用了三角形 。
and as it moves around , the electrical activity can pass from one of these cells to the next cell to keep track of where it is , so that it can use its own movements to know where it is in its environment .	當它移動時 , 電子活動可以從其中一個細胞傳遞到下一個細胞 , 一直追蹤它的位置 , 讓它可以利用它自己的動作來知道它的位置在它的環境中 。
do people have grid cells ?	人們有網格細胞嗎 ?
well because all of the gridlike firing patterns have the same axes of symmetry , the same orientations of grid , shown in orange here , it means that the net activity of all of the grid cells in a particular part of the brain should change according to whether we're running along these six directions or running along one of the six directions in between .	嗯 , 因為所有類似發射的圖案都有相同的對稱軸 , 這裡有相同的橘色方向 , 意思是 , 大腦中所有格細胞的淨活動應該要根據我們在這六個方向跑步的方向來改變 , 或在兩者之間的六個方向跑 。
so we can put people in an mri scanner and have them do a little video game like the one i showed you and look for this signal .	所以我們可以把人放進核磁共振造影機 , 讓他們做一個小小的電玩遊戲 , 像我給你們看的一樣 , 去尋找這個信號 。
and indeed , you do see it in the human entorhinal cortex , which is the same part of the brain that you see grid cells in rats .	的確 , 在人類的牙齒皮質中 , 它也是你在老鼠身上看到的電網細胞的一部分 。
so back to homer .	回到荷馬 。
he's probably remembering where his car was in terms of the distances and directions to extended buildings and boundaries around the location where he parked .	他可能還記得他的車位在距離和方向的位置 , 延伸到他停車的地方 。
and that would be represented by the firing of boundarydetecting cells .	由邊界偵測細胞的發射所代表 。
he's also remembering the path he took out of the car park , which would be represented in the firing of grid cells .	他還記得他從汽車公園走出來的道路 , 會被用在電網板的發射中 。
now both of these kinds of cells can make the place cells fire .	兩種細胞都可以讓位置細胞發射 。
and he can return to the location where he parked by moving so as to find where it is that best matches the firing pattern of the place cells in his brain currently with the stored pattern where he parked his car .	他可以回到他停下來的位置 , 讓他可以移動的位置 , 找到在他腦袋裡的位置細胞的位置圖案 , 和他停車的位置圖案 。
and that guides him back to that location irrespective of visual cues like whether his car's actually there .	這引導他回到那個視覺暗示的位置 , 像是他的車真的在那裡 。
maybe it's been towed .	也許它已經被動了 。
but he knows where it was , so he knows to go and get it .	但他知道它在哪裡 , 所以他知道要去哪裡去拿它 。
so beyond spatial memory , if we look for this gridlike firing pattern throughout the whole brain , we see it in a whole series of locations which are always active when we do all kinds of autobiographical memory tasks , like remembering the last time you went to a wedding , for example .	所以 , 除了空間記憶之外 , 如果我們在整個大腦中尋找類似的發射模式 , 我們會看到一系列的地點 , 當我們做各種自傳記憶任務時 , 比如記得你上次去參加婚禮時 , 都會活躍起來 。
so it may be that the neural mechanisms for representing the space around us are also used for generating visual imagery so that we can recreate the spatial scene , at least , of the events that have happened to us when we want to imagine them .	可能是 , 代表我們周圍的空間的神經機制也被用來產生視覺影像 , 這樣我們就可以重建空間場景 , 至少 , 當我們想想像它們時發生的事件 。
so if this was happening , your memories could start by place cells activating each other via these dense interconnections and then reactivating boundary cells to create the spatial structure of the scene around your viewpoint .	所以如果這發生了 , 你的記憶可以從細胞開始 , 透過這些密集的連結來啟動彼此 , 再回應邊界細胞 , 創造你周圍的景象空間結構 。
and grid cells could move this viewpoint through that space .	網格細胞可以透過這個空間移動這個觀點 。
another kind of cell , head direction cells , which i didn't mention yet , they fire like a compass according to which way you're facing .	另一種細胞 , 頭部方向細胞 , 我還沒提到 , 它們就像是你面臨的指南 。
they could define the viewing direction from which you want to generate an image for your visual imagery , so you can imagine what happened when you were at this wedding , for example .	他們可以從你想要為你的視覺產生一張圖片 , 你可以想像當你在這個婚禮上發生了什麼事 。
so this is just one example of a new era really in cognitive neuroscience where we're beginning to understand psychological processes like how you remember or imagine or even think in terms of the actions of the billions of individual neurons that make up our brains .	這只是一個新時代在認知神經科學中 , 我們開始了解心理學的過程 , 例如你如何記住或想像 , 甚至以數十億個獨立的神經元的行為來思考 。
thank you very much .	非常謝謝大家
imagine a global security driven by collaboration among agencies , government , the private sector and the public . that's not just the distant hope of opensource fans , it's the vision of james stavridis , the supreme commander of nato , who shares vivid moments from recent military history to explain why security of the future should be built with bridges rather than walls .	想像一下 , 全球安全是由政府、政府、私營部門和大眾所驅動的 , 這不僅僅是開放原始碼迷 , 是詹姆斯•史塔里迪斯的願景 , 納粹軍事史上最頂尖的指揮者 , 分享來自最近軍事歷史的偏遠時刻 , 來解釋未來的安全性 , 而不是牆壁 。
collaboration , global issues , opensource , peace , politics , social media , violence , war	合作、全球議題、開放原始碼、和平政治、社交媒體、暴力、戰爭、戰爭、戰爭 。
james stavridis: how nato's supreme commander thinks about global security	詹姆斯•史塔里斯:nato的最高指揮官認為全球安全性是如何的 ?
i'm gonna talk a little bit about opensource security , because we've got to get better at security in this 21st century .	我現在要談的是開放原始碼安全 , 因為在21世紀 , 我們必須在安全上更好 。
let me start by saying , let's look back to the 20th century , and kind of get a sense of how that style of security worked for us .	讓我先說 , 讓我們回頭看看二十世紀 , 看看安全的風格是如何為我們工作的 。
this is verdun , a battlefield in france just north of the nato headquarters in belgium .	這是verdun , 一個在法國北部的奈米總部的戰場 。
at verdun , in 1916 , over a 300day period , 700 , 000 people were killed , so about 2 , 000 a day .	1916年的verdun , 在1916年 , 超過300天 , 70萬人被殺害 , 一天大約有2 , 000人 。
if you roll it forward 20thcentury security into the second world war , you see the battle of stalingrad , 300 days , 2 million people killed .	如果你將它推向二十世紀的第二次世界大戰 , 你會看到史達丁堡的戰鬥 , 300天 , 兩百萬人死亡 。
we go into the cold war , and we continue to try and build walls .	我們進入冷戰中 , 我們持續嘗試建造牆壁 。
we go from the trench warfare of the first world war to the maginot line of the second world war , and then we go into the cold war , the iron curtain , the berlin wall .	我們從第一次世界大戰的角度 , 到第二次世界大戰的角度 , 接著我們進入冷戰 , 鐵幕 , 柏林牆 。
my thesis for us today is , instead of building walls to create security , we need to build bridges .	我今天的論點是 , 與其建造牆來建立安全 , 我們需要建立橋樑 。
this is a famous bridge in europe .	這是歐洲有名的橋 。
it's the bridge over the drina river , the subject of a novel by ivo andrić , and it talks about how , in that very troubled part of europe and the balkans , over time there's been enormous building of walls .	這座橋橫跨大西洋的大陸 , 一本小說的主題是 , 在歐洲和巴爾幹的地區 , 長久以來 , 牆壁是巨大的 。
more recently , in the last decade , we begin to see these communities start , hesitatingly , to come together .	最近 , 在過去十年 , 我們開始看到這些社區開始猶豫地團結起來 。
i would argue , again , opensource security is about connecting the international , the interagency , the privatepublic , and lashing it together with strategic communication , largely in social networks .	我會再次爭論 , 開放原始碼安全 , 即將國際、國際間、私人企業 , 將它與戰略通訊結合 , 主要是在社交網路上 。
so let me talk a little bit about why we need to do that , because our global commons is under attack in a variety of ways , and none of the sources of threat to the global commons will be solved by building walls .	讓我稍微談一下為何我們需要這麼做 , 因為我們的全球公有物以不同的方式攻擊 , 沒有任何威脅到全球公有物的來源會被建牆來解決 。
now , i'm a sailor , obviously .	顯然 , 我是個水手 。
this is a ship , a liner , clipping through the indian ocean .	這是一艘船 , 一艘船 , 橫跨印度洋 。
what's wrong with this picture ?	這張照片出了什麼問題 ?
it's got concertina wire along the sides of it .	它沿著它的側邊有凝固纖維 。
that's to prevent pirates from attacking it .	那就是防止海盜攻擊它 。
piracy is a very active threat today around the world . this is in the indian ocean .	皮拉西今天在世界各地是個非常活躍的威脅 。 這是在印度洋 。
piracy is also very active in the strait of malacca .	皮西在馬加拉卡的時代也是非常活躍的 。
it's active in the gulf of guinea .	它在幾內亞灣活躍 。
we see it in the caribbean .	我們在加勒比海看到了 。
it's a $10billionayear discontinuity in the global transport system .	在全球交通系統中 , 它是十億美元的不穩定性 。
last year , at this time , there were 20 vessels , 500 mariners held hostage .	去年 , 那裡有20艘船 , 500艘海軍主宰 。
this is an attack on the global commons .	這是針對全球公有物的攻擊 。
we need to think about how to address it .	我們需要思考如何處理它 。
let's shift to a different kind of sea , the cyber sea .	讓我們轉移到另一種海洋 , 網路海 。
here are photographs of two young men .	這是兩位年輕男性的照片 。
at the moment , they're incarcerated .	目前 , 他們被監禁了 。
they conducted a credit card fraud that netted them over 10 billion dollars .	他們做了一個信用卡詐欺 , 將他們網上超過一千億美金 。
this is part of cybercrime which is a $2trillionayear discontinuity in the global economy .	這是網路犯罪的一部分 , 它是全球經濟中2兆美元的連續性 。
two trillion a year .	一年有兩兆 。
that's just under the gdp of great britain .	這只是英國的國內生產總值 。
so this cyber sea , which we know endlessly is the fundamental piece of radical openness , is very much under threat as well .	這種網路海 , 我們無止盡的知道是徹底開放的一塊 , 對於威脅也是非常重要的 。
another thing i worry about in the global commons is the threat posed by trafficking , by the movement of narcotics , opium , here coming out of afghanistan through europe over to the united states .	在全球公有物中 , 我擔心的另一件事是人口販賣所造成的威脅 , 由毒品、鴉片 , 從阿富汗到美國 。
we worry about cocaine coming from the andean ridge north .	我們擔心可卡因來自安地斯山脊的北方 。
we worry about the movement of illegal weapons and trafficking . above all , perhaps , we worry about human trafficking , and the awful cost of it .	我們擔心非法武器的動作 , 最重要的是 , 也許 , 我們擔心人口販賣 , 以及它的成本 。
trafficking moves largely at sea but in other parts of the global commons .	人口販賣會在海上移動 , 但在全球公有物的其他部分 。
this is a photograph , and i wish i could tell you that this is a very hightech piece of us navy gear that we're using to stop the trafficking .	這是一張照片 , 我希望我能告訴各位 , 這是我們用來阻止人口販賣的高科技片段 。
the bad news is , this is a semisubmersible run by drug cartels .	壞消息是 , 這是一個半導體 , 可以用毒品軟骨來運作 。
it was built in the jungles of south america .	它是在南美叢林建造的 。
we caught it with that lowtech raft — — and it was carrying six tons of cocaine .	我們用那個低科技的強暴抓住它 , 它帶著六噸的可卡因 。
crew of four . sophisticated communications sweep .	四個 , 複雜的溝通 。
this kind of trafficking , in narcotics , in humans , in weapons , god forbid , in weapons of mass destruction , is part of the threat to the global commons .	這種在人體、人體、武器、上帝禁止、大規模毀滅的武器是全球公有物威脅的一部分 。
and let's pull it together in afghanistan today .	今天在阿富汗將它結合在一起 。
this is a field of poppies in afghanistan .	這是在阿富汗的小狗 。
eighty to 90 percent of the world's poppy , opium and heroin , comes out of afghanistan .	世界上百分之九十到九十的流浪、鴉片和海洛因 , 來自阿富汗 。
we also see there , of course , terrorism .	當然 , 我們也看到了恐怖主義 。
this is where al qaeda is staged from .	這是基地組織的所在 。
we also see a very strong insurgency embedded there .	我們也看到一個非常強烈的保險制度 。
so this terrorism concern is also part of the global commons , and what we must address .	所以 , 恐怖主義也是全球公有物的一部分 , 我們必須處理什麼 。
so here we are , 21st century .	這裡是21世紀 。
we know our 20thcentury tools are not going to work .	我們知道我們的二十世紀的工具不會成功 。
what should we do ?	我們該怎麼做 ?
i would argue that we will not deliver security solely from the barrel of a gun .	我會說 , 我們不會只靠槍支來遞送安全 。
we will not deliver security solely from the barrel of a gun .	我們不會只靠槍支來遞送安全 。
we will need the application of military force .	我們需要軍事力量的應用 。
when we do it , we must do it well , and competently .	當我們這樣做時 , 我們必須要做得很好 , 且能做到 。
but my thesis is , opensource security is about international , interagency , privatepublic connection pulled together by this idea of strategic communication on the internet .	但我的論點是 , 開放式安全是國際、國際間、私人的連結 , 由網路上策略性的溝通所構成 。
let me give you a couple of examples of how this works in a positive way .	讓我舉幾個例子 , 說明這如何用正面的方式運作 。
this is afghanistan . these are afghan soldiers .	這是阿富汗 , 這是阿富汗士兵 。
they are all holding books .	他們都握有書籍 。
you should say , " that's odd . i thought i read that this demographic , young men and women in their 20s and 30s , is largely illiterate in afghanistan . "	你應該說: 「 這很奇怪 。 我想我讀到 , 這種人口統計 , 年輕男女 , 她們二十、三十歲 , 大部分是在阿富汗 。 」
you would be correct .	你會是正確的 。
eightyfive percent cannot read when they enter the security forces of afghanistan .	當他們進入阿富汗的安全力量時 , 85%就無法閱讀 。
why ? because the taliban withheld education during the period of time in which these men and women would have learned to read .	為甚麼 ? 因為塔利班在時間的時期 , 受過教育 , 這些男性和女性會學會閱讀 。
so the question is , so , why are they all standing there holding books ?	所以 , 問題是 , 為什麼他們都站在那裡拿著書 ?
the answer is , we are teaching them to read in literacy courses by nato in partnership with private sector entities , in partnership with development agencies .	答案是 , 我們教導他們閱讀文學課程 , 由納多和私人機構合作 , 與發展機構合作 。
we've taught well over 200 , 000 afghan security forces to read and write at a basic level .	我們已經教導了超過二十萬人阿富汗的安全部隊 , 以基本的角度閱讀和寫字 。
when you can read and write in afghanistan , you will typically put a pen in your pocket .	當你可以在阿富汗閱讀和寫作 , 你通常會把一支筆放在口袋裡 。
at the ceremonies , when these young men and women graduate , they take that pen with great pride , and put it in their pocket .	在典禮上 , 當這些年輕男女畢業時 , 他們用大驕傲的鉛筆 , 把它放在他們的口袋裡 。
this is bringing together international — there are 50 nations involved in this mission — interagency — these development agencies — and privatepublic , to take on this kind of security .	這帶來了國際性的五十個國家 , 涉及了這個使命 , 國際發展機構 , 私人企業 , 採取這種安全 。
now , we are also teaching them combat skills , of course , but i would argue , opensource security means connecting in ways that create longer lasting security effect .	當然 , 我們也在教他們戰鬥技巧 , 但我認為 , 開放原始碼安全意味著將更長久的安全效應連結起來 。
this is a us navy warship .	這是一個美國海軍戰艦 。
it's called the comfort .	它叫做舒適感 。
there's a sister ship called the mercy .	有一艘叫 「 慈悲 」 的姐妹船 。
they are hospital ships .	他們是醫院的船隻 。
this one , the comfort , operates throughout the caribbean and the coast of south america conducting patient treatments .	這個是舒適的 , 在加勒比海和南美洲的海岸進行病人治療 。
on a typical cruise , they'll do 400 , 000 patient treatments .	在典型的情況下 , 他們會進行四十萬個病人治療 。
it is crewed not strictly by military but by a combination of humanitarian organizations: operation hope , project smile .	它不是被軍隊嚴格統治 , 而是透過人道組織的組合:行動希望、計畫微笑 。
other organizations send volunteers .	其他組織發送志願者 。
interagency physicians come out .	內科醫師出來了 。
they're all part of this .	它們都是其中的一部分 。
to give you one example of the impact this can have , this little boy , eight years old , walked with his mother two days to come to the eye clinic put on by the comfort .	給你一個例子 , 這個小男孩 , 八歲 , 帶著他媽兩天走到舒適的診所 。
when he was fitted , over his extremely myopic eyes , he suddenly looked up and said , " mama , veo el mundo . "	當他被配上時 , 穿過極為迷幻的眼睛 , 他突然抬頭看 , 說: 「 媽媽 , 維奧•艾爾•賈伯多 。 」
" mom , i see the world . "	「 媽 , 我看見世界 。 」
multiply this by 400 , 000 patient treatments , this privatepublic collaboration with security forces , and you begin to see the power of creating security in a very different way .	將之乘以四十萬個病人治療 , 這種私人合作和安全力量 , 你開始以非常不同的角度來看 , 創造安全的力量 。
here you see baseball players .	這裡你可以看到棒球選手 。
can you pick out the two us army soldiers in this photograph ?	你能在照片中挑出兩位美國軍人軍人嗎 ?
they are the two young men on either side of these young boys . this is part of a series of baseball clinics , where we have explored collaboration between major league baseball , the department of state , who sets up the diplomatic piece of this , military baseball players , who are real soldiers with real skills but participate in this mission , and they put on clinics throughout latin america and the caribbean , in honduras , in nicaragua , in all of the central american and caribbean nations where baseball is so popular , and it creates security .	他們是這兩位年輕男孩的兩方 。 這是一系列棒球診所的一部分 , 我們在南美和加勒比海的大聯盟、國家部門 , 他們設立了這個外交的軍事棒球員 , 他們是真正的軍事棒球員 , 他們有真正的技能 , 但參與了這個任務 , 他們在整個拉丁美洲和加勒比海和加勒比海和加勒比亞的診所 , 在全美和加勒比亞 , 在那裡 , 在全美和加勒比亞 , 創造出了軍 。
it shows role models to young men and women about fitness and about life that i would argue help create security for us .	它展現了年輕男女的榜樣 , 關於健身和生活 , 我會爭辯為我們創造安全 。
another aspect of this partnership is in disaster relief .	這種合作關係的另一個面向是災難的解救 。
this is a us air force helicopter participating after the tsunami in 2004 which killed 250 , 000 people .	這是美國空軍直升機在2004年抵達海嘯之後 , 殺死了25萬人 。
in each of these major disasters — the tsunami in 2004 , 250 , 000 dead , the kashmiri earthquake in pakistan , 2005 , 85 , 000 dead , the haitian earthquake , about 300 , 000 dead , more recently the awful earthquaketsunami combination which struck japan and its nuclear industry — in all of these instances , we see partnerships between international actors , interagency , privatepublic working with security forces to respond to this kind of natural disaster .	在每一個重大災難中 , 2004年的海嘯 , 25 , 000人死於巴基斯坦的卡許里地震 , 2005 , 85 , 000人死亡 , 海地地震 , 近期有30萬人死 , 更是可怕的地震 , 加上日本和其核產業 , 在所有這些情況下 , 我們看到國際演員之間的合作關係 , 國際演員 , 國際關係 , 私人和安全部隊合作 。
so these are examples of this idea of opensource security .	這些是開放原始碼安全的例子 。
we tie it together , increasingly , by doing things like this .	我們將它綁在一起 , 越來越多 , 做這樣的事 。
now , you're looking at this thinking , " ah , admiral , these must be sea lanes of communication , or these might be fiber optic cables . "	現在 , 你看著這個想法: 「 啊 , 不可思議 , 這些必定是溝通的海平線 , 或這些可能是光纖電纜 。 」
no . this is a graphic of the world according to twitter .	不 , 這張圖是twitter的世界 。
purple are tweets . green are geolocation .	紫色是推特 。 綠色是地分配 。
white is the synthesis .	白色是合成 。
it's a perfect evocation of that great population survey , the six largest nations in the world in descending order: china , india , facebook , the united states , twitter and indonesia .	這是個完美的進展 , 大人口調查 , 世界上六個最大的國家 , 下降秩序:中國、印度、臉書、美國、推特和印尼 。
why do we want to get in these nets ?	為什麼我們要用這些蚊帳 ?
why do we want to be involved ?	我們為什麼要參與其中 ?
we talked earlier about the arab spring , and the power of all this .	我們先前談到阿拉伯之春 , 及所有這一切的力量 。
i'll give you another example , and it's how you move this message .	我再舉另一個例子 , 就是你如何傳遞這個訊息 。
i gave a talk like this in london a while back about this point . i said , as i say to all of you , i'm on facebook . friend me .	我在倫敦舉辦了一場像這樣的演講 。 我說 , 正如我對你們所有人說的 , 我在臉書上 。 朋友我 。
got a little laugh from the audience .	聽眾有點笑 。
there was an article which was run by ap , on the wire .	有一篇文章是ap在電線上運作的 。
got picked up in two places in the world: finland and indonesia .	在世界上有兩個地方 , 芬蘭和印尼 。
the headline was: nato admiral needs friends .	標題是:北約的鄰居需要朋友 。
and the story was a catalyst , and the next morning i had hundreds of facebook friend requests from indonesians and finns , mostly saying , " admiral , we heard you need a friend , and oh , by the way , what is nato ? "	故事是一個催化劑 , 隔天早上 , 我有數百個臉書朋友 , 來自印尼人和芬 , 主要是說: 「 不正義 , 我們聽說你需要一個朋友 , 喔 , 順便一提 , 奈及利亞是什麼 ? 」
yeah , we laugh , but this is how we move the message , and moving that message is how we connect international , interagency , privatepublic , and these social nets to help create security .	沒錯 , 我們笑了 , 但這就是我們傳遞訊息的方式 , 傳遞訊息就是我們如何連結國際、國際間、私人企業 , 以及這些社交網 , 來協助創造安全 。
now , let me hit a somber note .	現在 , 讓我按下一個聲響 。
this is a photograph of a brave british soldier .	這是英國士兵的照片 。
he's in the scots guards .	他在蘇格蘭的守衛中 。
he's standing the watch in helmand , in southern afghanistan .	他站在阿富汗南部的海爾曼旁觀看 。
i put him here to remind us , i would not want anyone to leave the room thinking that we do not need capable , competent militaries who can create real military effect .	我讓他來這裡提醒我們 , 我不想讓任何人離開房間 , 認為我們不需要有能力、能創造出真正的軍事效應 。
that is the core of who we are and what we do , and we do it to protect freedom , freedom of speech , all the things we treasure in our societies .	這就是我們是誰和我們所做的核心 , 我們把它做成保護自由、言論自由、所有我們在社會中珍藏的東西 。
but , you know , life is not an onandoff switch .	但 , 你知道的 , 生命不是一個開關 。
you don't have to have a military that is either in hard combat or is in the barracks .	你不需要有軍隊 , 要麼在很困難的戰鬥中 , 要不就是在停車場 。
i would argue life is a rheostat .	我會說 , 生命是種隨機的 。
you have to dial it in , and as i think about how we create security in this 21st century , there will be times when we will apply hard power in true war and crisis , but there will be many instances , as we've talked about today , where our militaries can be part of creating 21stcentury security , international , interagency , privatepublic , connected with competent communication .	你得把它撥進去 , 想想我們如何在21世紀創造安全 , 將有時我們會在真正的戰爭和危機上施加強大的力量 , 但現在有很多的例子 , 我們的軍隊可以是創造21世紀安全、國際安全、國際間、公開、公開、私人的溝通 。
i would close by saying that we heard earlier today about wikipedia . i use wikipedia all the time to look up facts , and as all of you appreciate , wikipedia is not created by 12 brilliant people locked in a room writing articles .	最後我會說 , 今天我們聽說維基百科 。 我常常用維基百科檢查事實 , 你們都很欣賞維基 , 維基百科並不是由12位傑出的人鎖在房間裡寫文章 。
wikipedia , every day , is tens of thousands of people inputting information , and every day millions of people withdrawing that information .	維基百科 , 每天都有成千上萬的人在輸入資訊 , 每天有數百萬人打破這些資訊 。
it's a perfect image for the fundamental point that no one of us is as smart as all of us thinking together .	這對根本意義來說是完美的影像 , 沒有人像我們所有人一樣聰明 。
no one person , no one alliance , no one nation , no one of us is as smart as all of us thinking together .	沒有一個人 , 沒有一個聯盟 , 沒有一個國家 , 沒有一個人像我們所有人一樣聰明 。
the vision statement of wikipedia is very simple: a world in which every human being can freely share in the sum of all knowledge .	維基百科的願景很簡單:一個世界 , 每個人都可以自由分享在所有知識的總和中 。
my thesis for you is that by combining international , interagency , privatepublic , strategic communication , together , in this 21st century , we can create the sum of all security .	我的論點是 , 將國際、國際間、私人、戰略通訊結合在一起 , 在21世紀 , 我們可以創造所有安全的總和 。
thank you very much . thank you . thank you .	非常謝謝大家 。 謝謝 。 謝謝 。
